      <p><b>Madagascar</b> (<span class="rt-commentedText nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/Ë/: secondary stress follows">Ë</span><span title="'m' in 'my'">m</span><span title="/Ã¦/: 'a' in 'bad'">Ã¦</span><span title="'d' in 'dye'">d</span><span title="/É/: 'a' in 'about'">É</span><span title="/Ë/: primary stress follows">Ë</span><span title="/É¡/: 'g' in 'guy'">É¡</span><span title="/Ã¦/: 'a' in 'bad'">Ã¦</span><span title="'s' in 'sigh'">s</span><span title="'k' in 'kind'">k</span><span title="/Ér/: 'er' in 'letter'">Ér</span></span>,<span class="wrap"> </span>-<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="'k' in 'kind'">k</span><span title="/ÉËr/: 'ar' in 'far'">ÉËr</span></span>/</a></span></span>; <a href="/wiki/Malagasy_language" title="Malagasy language">Malagasy</a>: <i lang="mg">Madagasikara</i>), officially the <b>Republic of Madagascar</b> (Malagasy: <i lang="mg">Repoblikan'i Madagasikara</i>, <small>Malagasy pronunciation:&nbsp;</small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Malagasy" title="Help:IPA/Malagasy">[republiËkÊ²an madaÉ¡asËkÊ²arÉÌ¥]</a></span>; <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a>: <i lang="fr">RÃ©publique de Madagascar</i>), and previously known as the <b><a href="/wiki/Malagasy_Republic" title="Malagasy Republic">Malagasy Republic</a></b>, is an <a href="/wiki/Island_country" title="Island country">island country</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Indian_Ocean" title="Indian Ocean">Indian Ocean</a>, approximately 400 kilometres (250 miles) off the coast of <a href="/wiki/East_Africa" title="East Africa">East Africa</a> across the <a href="/wiki/Mozambique_Channel" title="Mozambique Channel">Mozambique Channel</a>. At 592,800 square kilometres (228,900&nbsp;sq&nbsp;mi) Madagascar is the world's second-largest <a href="/wiki/List_of_island_countries" title="List of island countries">island country</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-world-atlas_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-world-atlas-14">[14]</a></sup> The nation comprises the island of <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Madagascar" title="Geography of Madagascar">Madagascar</a> (the <a href="/wiki/List_of_islands_by_area" title="List of islands by area">fourth-largest island</a> in the world) and numerous smaller peripheral islands. Following the prehistoric breakup of the <a href="/wiki/Supercontinent" title="Supercontinent">supercontinent</a> <a href="/wiki/Gondwana" title="Gondwana">Gondwana</a>, Madagascar split from the <a href="/wiki/Indian_peninsula" class="mw-redirect" title="Indian peninsula">Indian subcontinent</a> around 88&nbsp;million years ago, allowing native plants and animals to evolve in relative isolation. Consequently, Madagascar is a <a href="/wiki/Biodiversity_hotspot" title="Biodiversity hotspot">biodiversity hotspot</a>; over 90% of <a href="/wiki/Wildlife_of_Madagascar" title="Wildlife of Madagascar">its wildlife</a> is found nowhere else on Earth. The island's diverse ecosystems and unique wildlife are threatened by the encroachment of the rapidly growing human population and other environmental threats. </p>
      <p>The archaeological evidence of the earliest human foraging on Madagascar may date up to 10,000 years ago.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup> Human settlement of Madagascar occurred by <a href="/wiki/Austronesian_peoples" title="Austronesian peoples">Austronesian peoples</a>, arriving on <a href="/wiki/Outrigger_canoe" class="mw-redirect" title="Outrigger canoe">outrigger canoes</a> from present-day <a href="/wiki/Indonesia" title="Indonesia">Indonesia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup> These were joined around the 9th century AD by <a href="/wiki/Bantu_peoples" title="Bantu peoples">Bantu</a> migrants crossing the Mozambique Channel from East Africa.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup> Other groups continued to settle on Madagascar over time, each one making lasting contributions to Malagasy cultural life. The <a href="/wiki/Malagasy_people" title="Malagasy people">Malagasy ethnic group</a> is often divided into 18 or more <a href="/wiki/Ethnic_groups_of_Madagascar" class="mw-redirect" title="Ethnic groups of Madagascar">subgroups</a>, of which the largest are the <a href="/wiki/Merina_people" title="Merina people">Merina</a> of the central highlands. </p>
      <p>Until the late 18th century, the island of Madagascar was ruled by a fragmented assortment of shifting sociopolitical alliances. Beginning in the early 19th century, most of the island was united and ruled as the <a href="/wiki/Merina_Kingdom" title="Merina Kingdom">Kingdom of Madagascar</a> by a <a href="/wiki/List_of_Malagasy_monarchs" class="mw-redirect" title="List of Malagasy monarchs">series</a> of Merina <a href="/wiki/Andriana" title="Andriana">nobles</a>. The monarchy ended in 1897 when the island was absorbed into the <a href="/wiki/French_colonial_empire" title="French colonial empire">French colonial empire</a>, from which the island gained independence in 1960. The autonomous state of Madagascar has since undergone four major constitutional periods, termed republics. Since 1992, the nation has officially been governed as a constitutional democracy from its capital at <a href="/wiki/Antananarivo" title="Antananarivo">Antananarivo</a>. However, in a <a href="/wiki/2009_Malagasy_political_crisis" title="2009 Malagasy political crisis">popular uprising in 2009</a>, president <a href="/wiki/Marc_Ravalomanana" title="Marc Ravalomanana">Marc Ravalomanana</a> was made to resign and presidential power was transferred in March 2009 to <a href="/wiki/Andry_Rajoelina" title="Andry Rajoelina">Andry Rajoelina</a>. Constitutional governance was restored in January 2014, when <a href="/wiki/Hery_Rajaonarimampianina" title="Hery Rajaonarimampianina">Hery Rajaonarimampianina</a> was named president following a <a href="/wiki/Malagasy_general_election,_2013" class="mw-redirect" title="Malagasy general election, 2013">2013 election</a> deemed fair and transparent by the international community. Madagascar is a member of the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a>, the <a href="/wiki/African_Union" title="African Union">African Union</a> (AU), the <a href="/wiki/Southern_African_Development_Community" title="Southern African Development Community">Southern African Development Community</a> (SADC), and the <a href="/wiki/Organisation_Internationale_de_la_Francophonie" class="mw-redirect" title="Organisation Internationale de la Francophonie">Organisation Internationale de la Francophonie</a>. </p>
      <p>Madagascar belongs to the group of least developed countries, according to the United Nations.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Malagasy_language" title="Malagasy language">Malagasy</a> and <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a> are both <a href="/wiki/Official_language" title="Official language">official languages</a> of the state. The majority of the population adheres to <a href="/wiki/Christianity_in_Madagascar" title="Christianity in Madagascar">Christianity</a>, <a href="/wiki/Malagasy_mythology" title="Malagasy mythology">traditional beliefs</a>, or an amalgamation of both. Ecotourism and agriculture, paired with greater investments in education, health, and private enterprise, are key elements of Madagascar's development strategy. Under Ravalomanana, these investments produced substantial economic growth, but the benefits were not evenly spread throughout the population, producing tensions over the increasing cost of living and declining living standards among the poor and some segments of the middle class. As of 2017<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Madagascar&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, the economy has been weakened by the 2009â2013 political crisis, and quality of life remains low for the majority of the Malagasy population. </p>

      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Madagascar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Etymology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <p>In the <a href="/wiki/Malagasy_language" title="Malagasy language">Malagasy language</a>, the island of Madagascar is called <i>Madagasikara</i> (<small>Malagasy pronunciation:&nbsp;</small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Malagasy" title="Help:IPA/Malagasy">[madaÉ¡asÊ²ËkÊ²arÉÌ¥]</a></span>) and its people are referred to as <i><a href="/wiki/Malagasy_people" title="Malagasy people">Malagasy</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-NatGeo1_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NatGeo1-19">[19]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-MalagasyOrNot_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MalagasyOrNot-20">[20]</a></sup> The island's appellation "Madagascar" is not of local origin but rather was popularized in the <a href="/wiki/Middle_Ages" title="Middle Ages">Middle Ages</a> by Europeans.<sup id="cite_ref-Cousins_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cousins-21">[21]</a></sup> The name <i>Madageiscar</i> was first recorded in the memoirs of 13th-century Venetian explorer <a href="/wiki/Marco_Polo" title="Marco Polo">Marco Polo</a> as a corrupted transliteration of the name <a href="/wiki/Mogadishu" title="Mogadishu">Mogadishu</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Somalia" title="Somalia">Somali</a> port with which Polo had confused the island.<sup id="cite_ref-Room_2006,_p._230_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Room_2006,_p._230-22">[22]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>On <a href="/wiki/Lawrence_of_Rome" class="mw-redirect" title="Lawrence of Rome">St. Laurence</a>'s Day in 1500, Portuguese explorer <a href="/wiki/Diogo_Dias" title="Diogo Dias">Diogo Dias</a> landed on the island and named it <i>SÃ£o LourenÃ§o</i>. Polo's name was preferred and popularized on <a href="/wiki/Renaissance" title="Renaissance">Renaissance</a> maps. No single Malagasy-language name predating <i>Madagasikara</i> appears to have been used by the local population to refer to the island, although some communities had their own name for part or all of the land they inhabited.<sup id="cite_ref-Room_2006,_p._230_22-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Room_2006,_p._230-22">[22]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Madagascar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Madagascar" title="Geography of Madagascar">Geography of Madagascar</a> and <a href="/wiki/Geology_of_Madagascar" title="Geology of Madagascar">Geology of Madagascar</a>
      </div> 
      <style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r978413945/mw-parser-output/.tmulti">.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbinner{display:flex;flex-direction:column}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .trow{display:flex;flex-direction:row;clear:left;flex-wrap:wrap;width:100%;box-sizing:border-box}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle{margin:1px;float:left}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .theader{clear:both;font-weight:bold;text-align:center;align-self:center;background-color:transparent;width:100%}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbcaption{background-color:transparent}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-left{text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-right{text-align:right}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-center{text-align:center}@media all and (max-width:720px){.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbinner{width:100%!important;box-sizing:border-box;max-width:none!important;align-items:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .trow{justify-content:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle{float:none!important;max-width:100%!important;box-sizing:border-box;text-align:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle .thumbcaption{text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .trow>.thumbcaption{text-align:center}}</style>
      <div class="thumb tmulti tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:378px;max-width:378px">
        <div class="trow">
         <div class="tsingle" style="width:182px;max-width:182px">
          <div class="thumbimage">
           <a href="/wiki/File:Imerina_countryside_riziere_rice_paddies_Madagascar.jpg" class="image"><img alt="terraced emerald paddy fields checker softly rolling hills" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Imerina_countryside_riziere_rice_paddies_Madagascar.jpg/180px-Imerina_countryside_riziere_rice_paddies_Madagascar.jpg" decoding="async" width="180" height="115" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Imerina_countryside_riziere_rice_paddies_Madagascar.jpg/270px-Imerina_countryside_riziere_rice_paddies_Madagascar.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Imerina_countryside_riziere_rice_paddies_Madagascar.jpg/360px-Imerina_countryside_riziere_rice_paddies_Madagascar.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1023" data-file-height="656"></a>
          </div>
         </div>
         <div class="tsingle" style="width:192px;max-width:192px">
          <div class="thumbimage">
           <a href="/wiki/File:Rainforestmadagascar04.tif" class="image"><img alt="Hills covered with dense blue green tropical forests" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/Rainforestmadagascar04.tif/lossless-page1-190px-Rainforestmadagascar04.tif.png" decoding="async" width="190" height="117" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/Rainforestmadagascar04.tif/lossless-page1-285px-Rainforestmadagascar04.tif.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/Rainforestmadagascar04.tif/lossless-page1-380px-Rainforestmadagascar04.tif.png 2x" data-file-width="1535" data-file-height="945"></a>
          </div>
         </div>
        </div>
        <div class="trow" style="display:flex">
         <div class="thumbcaption">
          The terraced paddy fields of the <a href="/wiki/Central_Highlands_(Madagascar)" title="Central Highlands (Madagascar)">central highlands</a> of Madagascar (left) give way to tropical rainforest along the eastern coast (right)
         </div>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>At 592,800 square kilometres (228,900&nbsp;sq&nbsp;mi),<sup id="cite_ref-BGNote_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BGNote-23">[23]</a></sup> Madagascar is the world's 47th <a href="/wiki/Largest_country" class="mw-redirect" title="Largest country">largest country</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-cia_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cia-24">[24]</a></sup> the 2nd largest <a href="/wiki/List_of_island_countries" title="List of island countries">island country</a><sup id="cite_ref-world-atlas_14-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-world-atlas-14">[14]</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/List_of_islands_by_area" title="List of islands by area">fourth-largest island</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-BGNote_23-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BGNote-23">[23]</a></sup> The country lies mostly between latitudes <a href="/wiki/12th_parallel_south" title="12th parallel south">12Â°S</a> and <a href="/wiki/26th_parallel_south" title="26th parallel south">26Â°S</a>, and longitudes <a href="/wiki/43rd_meridian_east" title="43rd meridian east">43Â°E</a> and <a href="/wiki/51st_meridian_east" title="51st meridian east">51Â°E</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-georeport_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-georeport-25">[25]</a></sup> Neighboring islands include the French territory of <a href="/wiki/R%C3%A9union" title="RÃ©union">RÃ©union</a> and the country of <a href="/wiki/Mauritius" title="Mauritius">Mauritius</a> to the east, as well as the state of <a href="/wiki/Comoros" title="Comoros">Comoros</a> and the French territory of <a href="/wiki/Mayotte" title="Mayotte">Mayotte</a> to the north west. The nearest mainland state is <a href="/wiki/Mozambique" title="Mozambique">Mozambique</a>, located to the west. </p>
      <p>The prehistoric breakup of the supercontinent <a href="/wiki/Gondwana" title="Gondwana">Gondwana</a> separated the MadagascarâAntarcticaâIndia landmass from the AfricaâSouth America landmass around 135&nbsp;million years ago. Madagascar later split from India about 88&nbsp;million years ago during the late <a href="/wiki/Cretaceous_period" class="mw-redirect" title="Cretaceous period">Cretaceous period</a> allowing plants and animals on the island to evolve in relative isolation.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Along the length of the eastern coast runs a narrow and steep <a href="/wiki/Escarpment" title="Escarpment">escarpment</a> containing much of the island's remaining tropical <a href="/wiki/Madagascar_lowland_forests" title="Madagascar lowland forests">lowland forest</a>. To the west of this ridge lies a <a href="/wiki/Plateau" title="Plateau">plateau</a> in the center of the island ranging in altitude from 750 to 1,500&nbsp;m (2,460 to 4,920&nbsp;ft) above sea level. These <a href="/wiki/Central_Highlands_(Madagascar)" title="Central Highlands (Madagascar)">central highlands</a>, traditionally the homeland of the <a href="/wiki/Merina_people" title="Merina people">Merina people</a> and the location of their historic capital at <a href="/wiki/Antananarivo" title="Antananarivo">Antananarivo</a>, are the most densely populated part of the island and are characterized by terraced, rice-growing valleys lying between grassy hills and patches of the <a href="/wiki/Madagascar_subhumid_forests" title="Madagascar subhumid forests">subhumid forests</a> that formerly covered the highland region. To the west of the highlands, the increasingly arid terrain gradually slopes down to the <a href="/wiki/Mozambique_Channel" title="Mozambique Channel">Mozambique Channel</a> and <a href="/wiki/Madagascar_mangroves" title="Madagascar mangroves">mangrove swamps</a> along the coast.<sup id="cite_ref-endemicstats_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-endemicstats-27">[27]</a></sup> </p> 
      <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r978413945/mw-parser-output/.tmulti">
      <div class="thumb tmulti tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:326px;max-width:326px">
        <div class="trow">
         <div class="tsingle" style="width:165px;max-width:165px">
          <div class="thumbimage">
           <a href="/wiki/File:Isalo_canyons.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Pastel striated stone outcroppings jut from the plains" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/Isalo_canyons.jpg/163px-Isalo_canyons.jpg" decoding="async" width="163" height="113" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/Isalo_canyons.jpg/245px-Isalo_canyons.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/Isalo_canyons.jpg/326px-Isalo_canyons.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2092" data-file-height="1452"></a>
          </div>
         </div>
         <div class="tsingle" style="width:157px;max-width:157px">
          <div class="thumbimage">
           <a href="/wiki/File:All%C3%A9e_des_Baobabs_near_Morondava,_Madagascar.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Giant baobabs clustered against the sky" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/All%C3%A9e_des_Baobabs_near_Morondava%2C_Madagascar.jpg/155px-All%C3%A9e_des_Baobabs_near_Morondava%2C_Madagascar.jpg" decoding="async" width="155" height="116" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/All%C3%A9e_des_Baobabs_near_Morondava%2C_Madagascar.jpg/233px-All%C3%A9e_des_Baobabs_near_Morondava%2C_Madagascar.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/All%C3%A9e_des_Baobabs_near_Morondava%2C_Madagascar.jpg/310px-All%C3%A9e_des_Baobabs_near_Morondava%2C_Madagascar.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1701" data-file-height="1276"></a>
          </div>
         </div>
        </div>
        <div class="trow" style="display:flex">
         <div class="thumbcaption">
          The grassy plains that dominate the western landscape are dotted with stony massifs (left), patches of deciduous forest, and <a href="/wiki/Avenue_of_the_Baobabs" title="Avenue of the Baobabs">baobab trees</a> (right), while the south is characterized by semi-desert and <a href="/wiki/Madagascar_spiny_thickets" class="mw-redirect" title="Madagascar spiny thickets">spiny forests</a>.
         </div>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Madagascar's highest peaks rise from three prominent highland <a href="/wiki/Massif" title="Massif">massifs</a>: <a href="/wiki/Maromokotro" title="Maromokotro">Maromokotro</a> 2,876&nbsp;m (9,436&nbsp;ft) in the <a href="/wiki/Tsaratanana_Massif#Tsaranoro_Massif" class="mw-redirect" title="Tsaratanana Massif">Tsaratanana Massif</a> is the island's highest point, followed by Boby Peak 2,658&nbsp;m (8,720&nbsp;ft) in the <a href="/wiki/Andringitra_Massif" title="Andringitra Massif">Andringitra Massif</a>, and Tsiafajavona 2,643&nbsp;m (8,671&nbsp;ft) in the <a href="/wiki/Ankaratra" title="Ankaratra">Ankaratra</a> Massif. To the east, the <i><a href="/wiki/Canal_des_Pangalanes" title="Canal des Pangalanes">Canal des Pangalanes</a></i> is a chain of human-made and natural lakes connected by canals built by the French just inland from the east coast and running parallel to it for some 600&nbsp;km (370&nbsp;mi).<sup id="cite_ref-EBLand_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EBLand-28">[28]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The western and southern sides, which lie in the <a href="/wiki/Rain_shadow" title="Rain shadow">rain shadow</a> of the central highlands, are home to <a href="/wiki/Madagascar_dry_deciduous_forests" title="Madagascar dry deciduous forests">dry deciduous forests</a>, <a href="/wiki/Madagascar_spiny_thickets" class="mw-redirect" title="Madagascar spiny thickets">spiny forests</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Deserts_and_xeric_shrublands" title="Deserts and xeric shrublands">deserts and xeric shrublands</a>. Due to their lower population densities, Madagascar's dry deciduous forests have been better preserved than the eastern rain forests or the original woodlands of the central plateau. The western coast features many protected harbors, but silting is a major problem caused by <a href="/wiki/Sediment" title="Sediment">sediment</a> from the high levels of inland <a href="/wiki/Erosion" title="Erosion">erosion</a> carried by rivers crossing the broad western plains.<sup id="cite_ref-EBLand_28-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EBLand-28">[28]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Madagascar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:332px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Koppen-Geiger_Map_MDG_present.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Koppen-Geiger_Map_MDG_present.svg/330px-Koppen-Geiger_Map_MDG_present.svg.png" decoding="async" width="330" height="238" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Koppen-Geiger_Map_MDG_present.svg/495px-Koppen-Geiger_Map_MDG_present.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Koppen-Geiger_Map_MDG_present.svg/660px-Koppen-Geiger_Map_MDG_present.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1181" data-file-height="850"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Koppen-Geiger_Map_MDG_present.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>A <a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="KÃ¶ppen climate classification">KÃ¶ppen climate classification</a> map of Madagascar
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Madagascar#Climate" title="Geography of Madagascar">Geography of Madagascar Â§&nbsp;Climate</a>
      </div> 
      <p>The combination of southeastern <a href="/wiki/Trade_winds" title="Trade winds">trade winds</a> and northwestern <a href="/wiki/Monsoons" class="mw-redirect" title="Monsoons">monsoons</a> produces a hot rainy season (NovemberâApril) with frequently destructive <a href="/wiki/Cyclone" title="Cyclone">cyclones</a>, and a relatively cooler dry season (MayâOctober). Rain clouds originating over the Indian Ocean discharge much of their moisture over the island's eastern coast; the heavy precipitation supports the area's <a href="/wiki/Rainforest" title="Rainforest">rainforest</a> ecosystem. The central highlands are both drier and cooler while the west is drier still, and a <a href="/wiki/Semi-arid_climate" title="Semi-arid climate">semi-arid climate</a> prevails in the southwest and southern interior of the island.<sup id="cite_ref-endemicstats_27-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-endemicstats-27">[27]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:332px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Biogeographic_timetable_of_Madagascar_-_journal.pone.0062086.g003.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Biogeographic_timetable_of_Madagascar_-_journal.pone.0062086.g003.png/330px-Biogeographic_timetable_of_Madagascar_-_journal.pone.0062086.g003.png" decoding="async" width="330" height="470" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Biogeographic_timetable_of_Madagascar_-_journal.pone.0062086.g003.png/495px-Biogeographic_timetable_of_Madagascar_-_journal.pone.0062086.g003.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Biogeographic_timetable_of_Madagascar_-_journal.pone.0062086.g003.png/660px-Biogeographic_timetable_of_Madagascar_-_journal.pone.0062086.g003.png 2x" data-file-width="2925" data-file-height="4163"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Biogeographic_timetable_of_Madagascar_-_journal.pone.0062086.g003.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Biogeographic timetable of Madagascar over the last 200 million years
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Tropical_cyclone" title="Tropical cyclone">Tropical cyclones</a> cause damage to infrastructure and local economies as well as loss of life.<sup id="cite_ref-LOC_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LOC-29">[29]</a></sup> In 2004, <a href="/wiki/Cyclone_Gafilo" title="Cyclone Gafilo">Cyclone Gafilo</a> became the strongest cyclone ever recorded to hit Madagascar. The storm killed 172 people, left 214,260 homeless<sup id="cite_ref-gafilo_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gafilo-30">[30]</a></sup> and caused more than US$250&nbsp;million in damage.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-31">[31]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ecology">Ecology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Madagascar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Ecology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Wildlife_of_Madagascar" title="Wildlife of Madagascar">Wildlife of Madagascar</a>, <a href="/wiki/Flora_of_Madagascar" title="Flora of Madagascar">Flora of Madagascar</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fauna_of_Madagascar" title="Fauna of Madagascar">Fauna of Madagascar</a>, <a href="/wiki/Agroecology_in_Madagascar" class="mw-redirect" title="Agroecology in Madagascar">Agroecology in Madagascar</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ecoregions_of_Madagascar" title="Ecoregions of Madagascar">Ecoregions of Madagascar</a>, and <a href="/wiki/List_of_World_Heritage_Sites_in_Madagascar" title="List of World Heritage Sites in Madagascar">List of World Heritage Sites in Madagascar</a>
      </div> 
      <p>As a result of the island's long isolation from neighboring continents, Madagascar is home to various plants and animals found nowhere else on Earth.<sup id="cite_ref-CIHotSpot_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIHotSpot-32">[32]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-tattersall_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tattersall-33">[33]</a></sup> Approximately 90% of all plant and animal species found in Madagascar are <a href="/wiki/Endemism" title="Endemism">endemic</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup> This distinctive ecology has led some ecologists to refer to Madagascar as the "eighth continent",<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup> and the island has been classified by <a href="/wiki/Conservation_International" title="Conservation International">Conservation International</a> as a biodiversity hotspot.<sup id="cite_ref-CIHotSpot_32-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIHotSpot-32">[32]</a></sup> Madagascar is classed as one of 17 <a href="/wiki/Megadiverse_countries" title="Megadiverse countries">megadiverse countries</a>. The country is home to seven terrestrial ecoregions: <a href="/wiki/Madagascar_lowland_forests" title="Madagascar lowland forests">Madagascar lowland forests</a>, <a href="/wiki/Madagascar_subhumid_forests" title="Madagascar subhumid forests">Madagascar subhumid forests</a>, <a href="/wiki/Madagascar_dry_deciduous_forests" title="Madagascar dry deciduous forests">Madagascar dry deciduous forests</a>, <a href="/wiki/Madagascar_ericoid_thickets" title="Madagascar ericoid thickets">Madagascar ericoid thickets</a>, <a href="/wiki/Madagascar_spiny_thickets" class="mw-redirect" title="Madagascar spiny thickets">Madagascar spiny thickets</a>, <a href="/wiki/Madagascar_succulent_woodlands" title="Madagascar succulent woodlands">Madagascar succulent woodlands</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Madagascar_mangroves" title="Madagascar mangroves">Madagascar mangroves</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-DinersteinOlson2017_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DinersteinOlson2017-36">[36]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>More than 80&nbsp;percent of Madagascar's 14,883 <a href="/wiki/Flora_of_Madagascar" title="Flora of Madagascar">plant species</a> are found nowhere else in the world, including five plant families.<sup id="cite_ref-endemism_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-endemism-37">[37]</a></sup> The family <i><a href="/wiki/Didiereaceae" title="Didiereaceae">Didiereaceae</a></i>, composed of four genera and 11 species, is limited to the <a href="/wiki/Madagascar_spiny_thickets" class="mw-redirect" title="Madagascar spiny thickets">spiny forests</a> of southwestern Madagascar.<sup id="cite_ref-endemicstats_27-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-endemicstats-27">[27]</a></sup> Four-fifths of the world's <i><a href="/wiki/Pachypodium" title="Pachypodium">Pachypodium</a></i> species are endemic to the island.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup> Three-fourths<sup id="cite_ref-B2011plant_39-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-B2011plant-39">[39]</a></sup> of Madagascar's 860<sup id="cite_ref-endemism_37-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-endemism-37">[37]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Orchid" class="mw-redirect" title="Orchid">orchid</a> species are found here alone, as are six of the world's nine <a href="/wiki/Adansonia" title="Adansonia">baobab</a> species.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup> The island is home to around 170 palm species, three times as many as on all of mainland Africa; 165 of them are endemic.<sup id="cite_ref-B2011plant_39-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-B2011plant-39">[39]</a></sup> Many native plant species are used as herbal remedies for a variety of afflictions. The drugs <a href="/wiki/Vinblastine" title="Vinblastine">vinblastine</a><sup id="cite_ref-MoleculesReview_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MoleculesReview-41">[41]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Vincristine" title="Vincristine">vincristine</a><sup id="cite_ref-MoleculesReview_41-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MoleculesReview-41">[41]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup> are <a href="/wiki/Vinca_alkaloid" title="Vinca alkaloid"><i>vinca</i> alkaloids</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup> used to treat <a href="/wiki/Hodgkin%27s_disease" class="mw-redirect" title="Hodgkin's disease">Hodgkin's disease</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Leukemia" title="Leukemia">leukemia</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup> and other cancers,<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup> were derived from the <a href="/wiki/Catharanthus" title="Catharanthus">Madagascar periwinkle</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-periw_49-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-periw-49">[49]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Ravenala_madagascariensis" class="mw-redirect" title="Ravenala madagascariensis">traveler's palm</a>, known locally as <i>ravinala</i><sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup> and endemic to the eastern rain forests,<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup> is highly iconic of Madagascar and is featured in the national emblem as well as the <a href="/wiki/Air_Madagascar" title="Air Madagascar">Air Madagascar</a> logo.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:OaklandZooLemurs.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Two ring-tailed lemurs curled up together" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/OaklandZooLemurs.jpg/220px-OaklandZooLemurs.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/OaklandZooLemurs.jpg/330px-OaklandZooLemurs.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/OaklandZooLemurs.jpg/440px-OaklandZooLemurs.jpg 2x" data-file-width="899" data-file-height="599"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:OaklandZooLemurs.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The <a href="/wiki/Ring-tailed_lemur" title="Ring-tailed lemur">ring-tailed lemur</a> is one of over 100 known species and subspecies of lemur found only in Madagascar.<sup id="cite_ref-2009Mittermeier_54-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2009Mittermeier-54">[54]</a></sup>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Like its flora, Madagascar's fauna is diverse and exhibits a high rate of endemism. Lemurs have been characterized as "Madagascar's flagship mammal species" by Conservation International.<sup id="cite_ref-CIHotSpot_32-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIHotSpot-32">[32]</a></sup> In the absence of monkeys and other competitors, these <a href="/wiki/Primate" title="Primate">primates</a> have adapted to a wide range of habitats and diversified into numerous species. As of 2012<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Madagascar&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, there were officially <a href="/wiki/List_of_lemur_species" title="List of lemur species">103 species and subspecies of lemur</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-lemurextinction_55-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lemurextinction-55">[55]</a></sup> 39 of which were described by zoologists between 2000 and 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-Mittermeier2008_56-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Mittermeier2008-56">[56]</a></sup> They are almost all classified as rare, vulnerable, or endangered. At least 17 species of lemur have become extinct since humans arrived on Madagascar, all of which were larger than the surviving lemur species.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>A number of other mammals, including the cat-like <a href="/wiki/Fossa_(animal)" title="Fossa (animal)">fossa</a>, are endemic to Madagascar. Over 300 species of birds have been recorded on the island, of which over 60&nbsp;percent (including four families and 42 genera) are endemic.<sup id="cite_ref-CIHotSpot_32-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIHotSpot-32">[32]</a></sup> The few families and genera of <a href="/wiki/Reptile" title="Reptile">reptile</a> that have reached Madagascar have diversified into more than 260 species, with over 90&nbsp;percent of these being endemic<sup id="cite_ref-Okajima_58-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Okajima-58">[58]</a></sup> (including one endemic family).<sup id="cite_ref-CIHotSpot_32-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIHotSpot-32">[32]</a></sup> The island is home to two-thirds of the world's <a href="/wiki/Chameleon" title="Chameleon">chameleon</a> species,<sup id="cite_ref-Okajima_58-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Okajima-58">[58]</a></sup> including the <a href="/wiki/Brookesia_micra" title="Brookesia micra">smallest known</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup> and researchers have proposed that Madagascar may be the origin of all chameleons. </p>
      <p>Endemic fish of Madagascar include two families, 15 genera and over 100 species, primarily inhabiting the island's freshwater lakes and rivers. Although invertebrates remain poorly studied in Madagascar, researchers have found high rates of endemism among the known species. All 651 species of terrestrial snail are endemic, as are a majority of the island's butterflies, <a href="/wiki/Scarabaeidae" title="Scarabaeidae">scarab beetles</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lacewing" class="mw-redirect" title="Lacewing">lacewings</a>, spiders, and dragonflies.<sup id="cite_ref-CIHotSpot_32-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIHotSpot-32">[32]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Environmental_issues">Environmental issues</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Madagascar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Environmental issues">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Deforestation_in_Madagascar" title="Deforestation in Madagascar">Deforestation in Madagascar</a> and <a href="/wiki/Illegal_logging_in_Madagascar" title="Illegal logging in Madagascar">Illegal logging in Madagascar</a>
      </div> 
      <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r978413945/mw-parser-output/.tmulti">
      <div class="thumb tmulti tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:204px;max-width:204px">
        <div class="trow">
         <div class="tsingle" style="width:202px;max-width:202px">
          <div class="thumbimage">
           <a href="/wiki/File:Manantenina_bushfire.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Burning Malagasy rainforest" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Manantenina_bushfire.jpg/200px-Manantenina_bushfire.jpg" decoding="async" width="200" height="141" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Manantenina_bushfire.jpg/300px-Manantenina_bushfire.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Manantenina_bushfire.jpg/400px-Manantenina_bushfire.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3072" data-file-height="2166"></a>
          </div>
         </div>
        </div>
        <div class="trow">
         <div class="tsingle" style="width:202px;max-width:202px">
          <div class="thumbimage">
           <a href="/wiki/File:Madagascar_erosion.jpg" class="image"><img alt="A vast, red soil gully caused by erosion" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Madagascar_erosion.jpg/200px-Madagascar_erosion.jpg" decoding="async" width="200" height="150" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Madagascar_erosion.jpg/300px-Madagascar_erosion.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Madagascar_erosion.jpg/400px-Madagascar_erosion.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1536"></a>
          </div>
         </div>
        </div>
        <div class="trow" style="display:flex">
         <div class="thumbcaption">
          Tavy (<a href="/wiki/Slash-and-burn" title="Slash-and-burn">slash-and-burn</a>) destruction of native forest habitat is widespread (Top), causing massive erosion (Bottom).
         </div>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Madagascar's varied fauna and flora are endangered by human activity.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup> Since the arrival of humans around 2,350&nbsp;years ago, Madagascar has lost more than 90&nbsp;percent of its original forest.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup> This forest loss is largely fueled by <i>tavy</i> ("fat"), a traditional <a href="/wiki/Slash-and-burn" title="Slash-and-burn">slash-and-burn</a> agricultural practice imported to Madagascar by the earliest settlers.<sup id="cite_ref-Gade_1996_62-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gade_1996-62">[62]</a></sup> Malagasy farmers embrace and perpetuate the practice not only for its practical benefits as an agricultural technique, but for its cultural associations with prosperity, health and venerated ancestral custom (<i>fomba malagasy</i>).<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup> As human population density rose on the island, deforestation accelerated beginning around 1,400 years ago.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated4_64-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated4-64">[64]</a></sup> By the 16th century, the central highlands had been largely cleared of their original forests.<sup id="cite_ref-Gade_1996_62-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gade_1996-62">[62]</a></sup> More recent contributors to the loss of forest cover include the growth in cattle herd size since their introduction around 1,000 years ago, a continued reliance on charcoal as a fuel for cooking, and the increased prominence of coffee as a <a href="/wiki/Cash_crop" title="Cash crop">cash crop</a> over the past century.<sup id="cite_ref-spittingwind_65-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-spittingwind-65">[65]</a></sup> Madagascar had a 2019 <a href="/wiki/Forest_Landscape_Integrity_Index" title="Forest Landscape Integrity Index">Forest Landscape Integrity Index</a> mean score of 4.63/10, ranking it 119th globally out of 172 countries.<sup id="cite_ref-FLII-Supplementary_66-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FLII-Supplementary-66">[66]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>According to a conservative estimate, about 40&nbsp;percent of the island's original forest cover was lost from the 1950s to 2000, with a thinning of remaining forest areas by 80&nbsp;percent.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup> In addition to traditional agricultural practice, wildlife conservation is challenged by the illicit harvesting of protected forests, as well as the state-sanctioned harvesting of precious woods within national parks. Although banned by then-President <a href="/wiki/Marc_Ravalomanana" title="Marc Ravalomanana">Marc Ravalomanana</a> from 2000 to 2009, the collection of small quantities of precious timber from national parks was re-authorized in January 2009 and dramatically intensified under the administration of <a href="/wiki/Andry_Rajoelina" title="Andry Rajoelina">Andry Rajoelina</a> as a key source of state revenues to offset cuts in donor support following Ravalomanana's ousting.<sup id="cite_ref-CrossroadsMarcus_68-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CrossroadsMarcus-68">[68]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><span class="anchor" id="Invasive_species"></span>Invasive species have likewise been introduced by human populations. Following the 2014 discovery in Madagascar of the <a href="/wiki/Duttaphrynus_melanostictus" title="Duttaphrynus melanostictus">Asian common toad</a>, a relative of a toad species that has severely harmed wildlife in Australia since the 1930s, researchers warned the toad could "wreak havoc on the country's unique fauna."<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup> Habitat destruction and hunting have threatened many of Madagascar's endemic species or driven them to extinction. The island's <a href="/wiki/Elephant_bird" title="Elephant bird">elephant birds</a>, a family of endemic giant <a href="/wiki/Ratite" title="Ratite">ratites</a>, became extinct in the 17th century or earlier, most probably because of human hunting of adult birds and poaching of their large eggs for food.<sup id="cite_ref-Davies_70-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Davies-70">[70]</a></sup> Numerous <a href="/wiki/Subfossil_lemur" title="Subfossil lemur">giant lemur</a> species vanished with the arrival of human settlers to the island, while others became extinct over the course of the centuries as a growing human population put greater pressures on lemur habitats and, among some populations, increased the rate of lemur hunting for food.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup> A July 2012 assessment found that the exploitation of natural resources since 2009 has had dire consequences for the island's wildlife: 90&nbsp;percent of lemur species were found to be threatened with extinction, the highest proportion of any mammalian group. Of these, 23 species were classified as critically endangered. By contrast, a previous study in 2008 had found only 38&nbsp;percent of lemur species were at risk of extinction.<sup id="cite_ref-lemurextinction_55-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lemurextinction-55">[55]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 2003, Ravalomanana announced the Durban Vision, an initiative to more than triple the island's <a href="/wiki/National_parks_of_Madagascar" class="mw-redirect" title="National parks of Madagascar">protected natural areas</a> to over 60,000&nbsp;km<sup>2</sup> (23,000&nbsp;sq&nbsp;mi) or 10&nbsp;percent of Madagascar's land surface. As of 2011<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Madagascar&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, areas protected by the state included five Strict Nature Reserves (<i>RÃ©serves Naturelles IntÃ©grales</i>), 21 Wildlife Reserves (<i>RÃ©serves SpÃ©ciales</i>) and 21 National Parks (<i>Parcs Nationaux</i>).<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup> In 2007 six of the national parks were declared a joint <a href="/wiki/List_of_World_Heritage_Sites_in_Madagascar" title="List of World Heritage Sites in Madagascar">World Heritage Site</a> under the name <a href="/wiki/Rainforests_of_the_Atsinanana" title="Rainforests of the Atsinanana">Rainforests of the Atsinanana</a>. These parks are <a href="/wiki/Marojejy_National_Park" title="Marojejy National Park">Marojejy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Masoala_National_Park" title="Masoala National Park">Masoala</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ranomafana_National_Park" title="Ranomafana National Park">Ranomafana</a>, <a href="/wiki/Zahamena_National_Park" title="Zahamena National Park">Zahamena</a>, <a href="/wiki/Andohahela_National_Park" title="Andohahela National Park">Andohahela</a> and <a href="/wiki/Andringitra_National_Park" title="Andringitra National Park">Andringitra</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup> Local timber merchants are harvesting scarce species of rosewood trees from protected rainforests within Marojejy National Park and exporting the wood to China for the production of luxury furniture and musical instruments.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup> To raise public awareness of Madagascar's environmental challenges, the <a href="/wiki/Wildlife_Conservation_Society" title="Wildlife Conservation Society">Wildlife Conservation Society</a> opened an exhibit entitled "<i>Madagascar!</i>" in June 2008 at the <a href="/wiki/Bronx_Zoo" title="Bronx Zoo">Bronx Zoo</a> in New York.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Madagascar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Madagascar" title="History of Madagascar">History of Madagascar</a>
      </div> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_period">Early period</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Madagascar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Early period">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Malagasy_girls_Madagascar_Merina.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/Malagasy_girls_Madagascar_Merina.jpg/220px-Malagasy_girls_Madagascar_Merina.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/Malagasy_girls_Madagascar_Merina.jpg/330px-Malagasy_girls_Madagascar_Merina.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/Malagasy_girls_Madagascar_Merina.jpg/440px-Malagasy_girls_Madagascar_Merina.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4288" data-file-height="2848"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Malagasy_girls_Madagascar_Merina.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Malagasy_people" title="Malagasy people">Malagasy</a> ancestry reflects a blend of Southeast Asian and Bantu (East African) roots.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Archaeological finds such as cut marks on bones found in the northwest and stone tools in the northeast indicate that Madagascar was visited by foragers around 2000&nbsp;BC.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup> Early <a href="/wiki/Holocene" title="Holocene">Holocene</a> humans might have existed on the island 10,500 years ago, based on grooves found on <a href="/wiki/Elephant_bird" title="Elephant bird">elephant bird</a> bones left by humans.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup> However, a counterstudy concluded that human-made marks date to 1,200 years ago at the earliest, in which the previously mentioned bone damage may have been made by scavengers, ground movements or cuts from the excavation process.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Traditionally, archaeologists have estimated that the earliest settlers arrived in successive waves in <a href="/wiki/Outrigger_canoe" class="mw-redirect" title="Outrigger canoe">outrigger canoes</a> from <a href="/wiki/Sunda_Islands" title="Sunda Islands">the Sunda islands</a> (<a href="/wiki/Malay_Archipelago" title="Malay Archipelago">Malay Archipelago</a>) possibly throughout the period between 350&nbsp;BC and 550&nbsp;AD, while others are cautious about dates earlier than 250&nbsp;AD. In either case, these dates make Madagascar the last major landmass on Earth to be settled by humans, except for <a href="/wiki/Iceland" title="Iceland">Iceland</a> and <a href="/wiki/New_Zealand" title="New Zealand">New Zealand</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup> It is proposed that <a href="/wiki/Ma%27anyan_people" title="Ma'anyan people">Ma'anyan people</a> were brought as laborers and slaves by <a href="/wiki/Malays_(ethnic_group)" title="Malays (ethnic group)">Malay</a> and <a href="/wiki/Javanese_people" title="Javanese people">Javanese people</a> in their trading fleets to Madagascar.<sup id="cite_ref-Dewar19932_81-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dewar19932-81">[81]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Burney20042_82-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Burney20042-82">[82]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Upon arrival, early settlers practiced slash-and-burn agriculture to clear the coastal rainforests for cultivation. The first settlers encountered Madagascar's abundance of megafauna, including <a href="/wiki/Subfossil_lemur" title="Subfossil lemur">giant lemurs</a>, <a href="/wiki/Elephant_bird" title="Elephant bird">elephant birds</a>, <a href="/wiki/Giant_fossa" class="mw-redirect" title="Giant fossa">giant fossa</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Malagasy_hippopotamus" title="Malagasy hippopotamus">Malagasy hippopotamus</a>, which have since become extinct because of hunting and habitat destruction.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup> By 600&nbsp;AD, groups of these early settlers had begun clearing the forests of the central highlands.<sup id="cite_ref-Camp93_85-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Camp93-85">[85]</a></sup> Arab traders first reached the island between the 7th and 9th centuries.<sup id="cite_ref-Wink_86-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Wink-86">[86]</a></sup> A wave of <a href="/wiki/Bantu_languages" title="Bantu languages">Bantu</a>-speaking migrants from southeastern Africa arrived around 1000&nbsp;AD.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup> South Indian Tamil merchants arrived around 11th century. They introduced the <a href="/wiki/Zebu" title="Zebu">zebu</a>, a type of long-horned humped cattle, which they kept in large herds.<sup id="cite_ref-Gade_1996_62-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gade_1996-62">[62]</a></sup> Irrigated paddy fields were developed in the central highland <a href="/wiki/Betsileo" class="mw-redirect" title="Betsileo">Betsileo</a> Kingdom and were extended with terraced paddies throughout the neighboring Kingdom of <a href="/wiki/Imerina" class="mw-redirect" title="Imerina">Imerina</a> a century later.<sup id="cite_ref-Camp93_85-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Camp93-85">[85]</a></sup> The rising intensity of land cultivation and the ever-increasing demand for zebu pasturage had largely transformed the central highlands from a forest ecosystem to grassland by the 17th century.<sup id="cite_ref-Gade_1996_62-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gade_1996-62">[62]</a></sup> The oral histories of the Merina people, who may have arrived in the central highlands between 600 and 1,000 years ago, describe encountering an established population they called the <a href="/wiki/Vazimba" title="Vazimba">Vazimba</a>. Probably the descendants of an earlier and less technologically advanced Austronesian settlement wave, the Vazimba were assimilated or expelled from the highlands by the Merina kings <a href="/wiki/Andriamanelo" title="Andriamanelo">Andriamanelo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ralambo" title="Ralambo">Ralambo</a> and <a href="/wiki/Andrianjaka" title="Andrianjaka">Andrianjaka</a> in the 16th and early 17th centuries.<sup id="cite_ref-vazimbadjp_88-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-vazimbadjp-88">[88]</a></sup> Today, the spirits of the Vazimba are revered as <i>tompontany</i> (ancestral masters of the land) by many traditional Malagasy communities.<sup id="cite_ref-Mythe_89-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Mythe-89">[89]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Arab_and_Portuguese_contacts">Arab and Portuguese contacts</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Madagascar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Arab and Portuguese contacts">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Detail_of_Diogo_Dias%27s_ship_(Cabral_Armada).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Detail_of_Diogo_Dias%27s_ship_%28Cabral_Armada%29.jpg/220px-Detail_of_Diogo_Dias%27s_ship_%28Cabral_Armada%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="222" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Detail_of_Diogo_Dias%27s_ship_%28Cabral_Armada%29.jpg/330px-Detail_of_Diogo_Dias%27s_ship_%28Cabral_Armada%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Detail_of_Diogo_Dias%27s_ship_%28Cabral_Armada%29.jpg/440px-Detail_of_Diogo_Dias%27s_ship_%28Cabral_Armada%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="587" data-file-height="592"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Detail_of_Diogo_Dias%27s_ship_(Cabral_Armada).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>European contact began in 1500 when <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_discoveries" title="Portuguese discoveries">Portuguese explorer</a> <a href="/wiki/Diogo_Dias" title="Diogo Dias">Diogo Dias</a> recorded the island while participating in the <a href="/wiki/2nd_Portuguese_India_Armada_(Cabral,_1500)" title="2nd Portuguese India Armada (Cabral, 1500)">2nd Portuguese India Armadas</a>.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Madagascar was an important transoceanic trading hub connecting ports of the Indian Ocean in the early centuries following human settlement. </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Recorded_history" title="Recorded history">written history</a> of Madagascar began with the Arabs, who established trading posts along the northwest coast by at least the 10th century and introduced <a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">Islam</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Arabic_script" title="Arabic script">Arabic script</a> (used to transcribe the Malagasy language in a form of writing known as <i><a href="/wiki/Sorabe" class="mw-redirect" title="Sorabe">sorabe</a></i>), Arab astrology, and other cultural elements.<sup id="cite_ref-LOC_29-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LOC-29">[29]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Portuguese">Portuguese</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Madagascar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Portuguese">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p>European contact began in 1500, when the <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Empire" title="Portuguese Empire">Portuguese</a> sea captain <a href="/wiki/Diogo_Dias" title="Diogo Dias">Diogo Dias</a> sighted the island, while participating in the <a href="/wiki/2nd_Portuguese_India_Armada_(Cabral,_1500)" title="2nd Portuguese India Armada (Cabral, 1500)">2nd Armada</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_India_Armadas" title="Portuguese India Armadas">Portuguese India Armadas</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-BGNote_23-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BGNote-23">[23]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Sainte_Luce_Reserve" title="Sainte Luce Reserve">Matatana</a> was the first Portuguese settlement on the south coast, 10 km west of <a href="/wiki/Fort_Dauphin_(Madagascar)" class="mw-redirect" title="Fort Dauphin (Madagascar)">Fort Dauphin</a>. In 1508, settlers there built a tower, a small village, and a stone column. This settlement was established in 1613 at the behest of the viceroy of <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_India" title="Portuguese India">Portuguese India</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jer%C3%B3nimo_de_Azevedo" title="JerÃ³nimo de Azevedo">Jeronimo de Azevedo</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_90-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-90">[90]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Matatana.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Matatana.jpg/220px-Matatana.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="144" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Matatana.jpg/330px-Matatana.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Matatana.jpg/440px-Matatana.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3227" data-file-height="2109"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Matatana.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Matatana, represented in a picture of 1613, regarding a settlement of the beginning of the 16th century, in the Book of Humberto LeitÃ£o"
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Contacts continued from the 1550s. Several colonization and conversion missions were ordered by King <a href="/wiki/John_III_of_Portugal" title="John III of Portugal">JoÃ£o III</a> and by the Viceroy of India, including one in 1553 by Baltazar Lobo de Sousa. In that mission, according to detailed descriptions by chroniclers Diogo do Couto and JoÃ£o de Barros, emissaries reached the inland via rivers and bays, exchanging goods and even converting one of the local kings.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="French">French</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Madagascar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: French">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p>The French established trading posts along the east coast in the late 17th century.<sup id="cite_ref-LOC_29-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LOC-29">[29]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>From about 1774 to 1824, Madagascar gained prominence among pirates and European traders, particularly those involved in the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_slave_trade" title="Atlantic slave trade">trans-Atlantic slave trade</a>. The small island of <a href="/wiki/%C3%8Ele_Sainte-Marie" title="Ãle Sainte-Marie">Nosy Boroha</a> off the northeastern coast of Madagascar has been proposed by some historians as the site of the legendary pirate utopia of <a href="/wiki/Libertalia" class="mw-redirect" title="Libertalia">Libertalia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup> Many European sailors were shipwrecked on the coasts of the island, among them <a href="/wiki/Robert_Drury_(sailor)" title="Robert Drury (sailor)">Robert Drury</a>, whose journal is one of the few written depictions of life in southern Madagascar during the 18th century.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The wealth generated by maritime trade spurred the rise of organized kingdoms on the island, some of which had grown quite powerful by the 17th century.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">[94]</a></sup> Among these were the <a href="/wiki/Betsimisaraka_people" title="Betsimisaraka people">Betsimisaraka</a> alliance of the eastern coast and the <a href="/wiki/Sakalava" class="mw-redirect" title="Sakalava">Sakalava</a> chiefdoms of <a href="/wiki/Menabe" title="Menabe">Menabe</a> and <a href="/wiki/Boina_Kingdom" title="Boina Kingdom">Boina</a> on the west coast. The Kingdom of Imerina, located in the central highlands with its capital at the <a href="/wiki/Rova_of_Antananarivo" title="Rova of Antananarivo">royal palace</a> of Antananarivo, emerged at around the same time under the leadership of King Andriamanelo.<sup id="cite_ref-Ogot_95-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ogot-95">[95]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Kingdom_of_Madagascar">Kingdom of Madagascar</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Madagascar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Kingdom of Madagascar">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Merina_Kingdom" title="Merina Kingdom">Merina Kingdom</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Andrianampoinimerina.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Andrianampoinimerina.jpg/170px-Andrianampoinimerina.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="211" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Andrianampoinimerina.jpg/255px-Andrianampoinimerina.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Andrianampoinimerina.jpg/340px-Andrianampoinimerina.jpg 2x" data-file-width="398" data-file-height="495"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Andrianampoinimerina.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>King <a href="/wiki/Andrianampoinimerina" title="Andrianampoinimerina">Andrianampoinimerina</a> (1787â1810)
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Upon its emergence in the early 17th century, the highland kingdom of Imerina was initially a minor power relative to the larger coastal kingdoms<sup id="cite_ref-Ogot_95-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ogot-95">[95]</a></sup> and grew even weaker in the early 18th century when King <a href="/wiki/Andriamasinavalona" title="Andriamasinavalona">Andriamasinavalona</a> divided it among his four sons. Following almost a century of warring and famine, Imerina was reunited in 1793 by King <a href="/wiki/Andrianampoinimerina" title="Andrianampoinimerina">Andrianampoinimerina</a> (1787â1810).<sup id="cite_ref-Hodder_96-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hodder-96">[96]</a></sup> From his initial capital <a href="/wiki/Ambohimanga" title="Ambohimanga">Ambohimanga</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">[97]</a></sup> and later from the <a href="/wiki/Rova_of_Antananarivo" title="Rova of Antananarivo">Rova of Antananarivo</a>, this Merina king rapidly expanded his rule over neighboring principalities. His ambition to bring the entire island under his control was largely achieved by his son and successor, King <a href="/wiki/Radama_I" title="Radama I">Radama I</a> (1810â28), who was recognized by the British government as King of Madagascar. Radama concluded a treaty in 1817 with the British governor of <a href="/wiki/Mauritius" title="Mauritius">Mauritius</a> to abolish the lucrative slave trade in return for British military and financial assistance. Artisan missionary envoys from the <a href="/wiki/London_Missionary_Society" title="London Missionary Society">London Missionary Society</a> began arriving in 1818 and included such key figures as <a href="/wiki/James_Cameron_(missionary)" title="James Cameron (missionary)">James Cameron</a>, <a href="/wiki/David_Jones_(missionary)" title="David Jones (missionary)">David Jones</a> and <a href="/wiki/David_Griffiths_(missionary)" title="David Griffiths (missionary)">David Griffiths</a>, who established schools, transcribed the <a href="/wiki/Malagasy_language" title="Malagasy language">Malagasy language</a> using the <a href="/wiki/Latin_alphabet" title="Latin alphabet">Roman alphabet</a>, translated the Bible, and introduced a variety of new technologies to the island.<sup id="cite_ref-Ade_Ajayi_1998,_pp._413â422_98-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ade_Ajayi_1998,_pp._413â422-98">[98]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Radama's successor, Queen <a href="/wiki/Ranavalona_I" title="Ranavalona I">Ranavalona I</a> (1828â61), responded to increasing political and cultural encroachment on the part of Britain and France by issuing a royal edict prohibiting the practice of <a href="/wiki/Christianity_in_Madagascar" title="Christianity in Madagascar">Christianity in Madagascar</a> and pressuring most foreigners to leave the territory. <a href="/wiki/William_Ellis_(missionary)" title="William Ellis (missionary)">William Ellis (missionary)</a> described his visits made during her reign in his book <i>Three Visits to Madagascar during the years 1853, 1854 and 1856</i>. The Queen made heavy use of the traditional practice of <i><a href="/wiki/Corv%C3%A9e" title="CorvÃ©e">fanompoana</a></i> (forced labor as tax payment) to complete public works projects and develop a standing army of between 20,000 and 30,000 <a href="/wiki/Merina" class="mw-redirect" title="Merina">Merina</a> soldiers, whom she deployed to pacify outlying regions of the island and further expand the Kingdom of Merina to encompass most of Madagascar. Residents of Madagascar could accuse one another of various crimes, including theft, Christianity and especially witchcraft, for which the ordeal of <i><a href="/wiki/Tangena" title="Tangena">tangena</a></i> was routinely obligatory. Between 1828 and 1861, the <i>tangena</i> ordeal caused about 3,000 deaths annually. In 1838, it was estimated that as many as 100,000 people in Imerina died as a result of the tangena ordeal, constituting roughly 20 percent of the population.<sup id="cite_ref-Stats_99-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Stats-99">[99]</a></sup> The combination of regular warfare, disease, difficult forced labor and harsh measures of justice resulted in a high mortality rate among soldiers and civilians alike during her 33-year reign, the population of Madagascar is estimated to have declined from around 5&nbsp;million to 2.5&nbsp;million between 1833 and 1839.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">[100]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Among those who continued to reside in Imerina were <a href="/wiki/Jean_Laborde" title="Jean Laborde">Jean Laborde</a>, an entrepreneur who developed munitions and other industries on behalf of the monarchy, and <a href="/wiki/Joseph-Fran%C3%A7ois_Lambert" title="Joseph-FranÃ§ois Lambert">Joseph-FranÃ§ois Lambert</a>, a French adventurer and slave trader, with whom then-Prince <a href="/wiki/Radama_II" title="Radama II">Radama II</a> signed a controversial trade agreement termed the Lambert Charter. Succeeding his mother, Radama II (1861â63) attempted to relax the queen's stringent policies, but was <a href="/wiki/Radama_II#Assassination_plot" title="Radama II">overthrown</a> two years later by Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Rainivoninahitriniony" title="Rainivoninahitriniony">Rainivoninahitriniony</a> (1852â1865) and an alliance of <i><a href="/wiki/Andriana" title="Andriana">Andriana</a></i> (noble) and <i><a href="/wiki/Hova_(Madagascar)" title="Hova (Madagascar)">Hova</a></i> (commoner) courtiers, who sought to end the absolute power of the monarch.<sup id="cite_ref-LOC_29-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LOC-29">[29]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Following the coup, the courtiers offered Radama's queen, <a href="/wiki/Rasoherina" title="Rasoherina">Rasoherina</a> (1863â68), the opportunity to rule, if she would accept a power sharing arrangement with the Prime Minister: a new social contract that would be sealed by a political marriage between them.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">[101]</a></sup> Queen Rasoherina accepted, first marrying Rainivoninahitriniony, then later deposing him and marrying his brother, Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Rainilaiarivony" title="Rainilaiarivony">Rainilaiarivony</a> (1864â95), who would go on to marry Queen <a href="/wiki/Ranavalona_II" title="Ranavalona II">Ranavalona II</a> (1868â83) and Queen <a href="/wiki/Ranavalona_III" title="Ranavalona III">Ranavalona III</a> (1883â97) in succession.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">[102]</a></sup> Over the course of Rainilaiarivony's 31-year tenure as prime minister, numerous policies were adopted to modernize and consolidate the power of the central government.<sup id="cite_ref-TA910_103-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TA910-103">[103]</a></sup> Schools were constructed throughout the island and attendance was made mandatory. Army organization was improved and British consultants were employed to train and professionalize soldiers.<sup id="cite_ref-FFO522_104-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FFO522-104">[104]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Polygamy" title="Polygamy">Polygamy</a> was outlawed and Christianity, declared the official religion of the court in 1869, was adopted alongside traditional beliefs among a growing portion of the populace.<sup id="cite_ref-TA910_103-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TA910-103">[103]</a></sup> Legal codes were reformed on the basis of British <a href="/wiki/Common_law" title="Common law">common law</a> and three European-style courts were established in the capital city.<sup id="cite_ref-FFO522_104-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FFO522-104">[104]</a></sup> In his joint role as Commander-in-Chief, Rainilaiarivony also successfully ensured the defense of Madagascar against several French colonial incursions.<sup id="cite_ref-FFO522_104-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FFO522-104">[104]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="French_colonization">French colonization</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Madagascar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: French colonization">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:LaGuerreAMadagascar.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/LaGuerreAMadagascar.jpg/170px-LaGuerreAMadagascar.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="256" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/LaGuerreAMadagascar.jpg/255px-LaGuerreAMadagascar.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/LaGuerreAMadagascar.jpg/340px-LaGuerreAMadagascar.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5300" data-file-height="7976"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:LaGuerreAMadagascar.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>A French poster about the <a href="/wiki/Franco-Hova_Wars" title="Franco-Hova Wars">Franco-Hova War</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>

      </div>
