       See also: <a href="/wiki/Madagascar_in_World_War_II" title="Madagascar in World War II">Madagascar in World War II</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Primarily on the basis that the Lambert Charter had not been respected, France invaded Madagascar in 1883 in what became known as the first <a href="/wiki/Franco-Hova_War" class="mw-redirect" title="Franco-Hova War">Franco-Hova War</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Boogaerde_p7_105-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Boogaerde_p7-105">[105]</a></sup> At the end of the war, Madagascar ceded the northern port town of <a href="/wiki/Antsiranana" title="Antsiranana">Antsiranana</a> (Diego Suarez) to France and paid 560,000 francs to Lambert's heirs.<sup id="cite_ref-Randier_p400_106-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Randier_p400-106">[106]</a></sup> In 1890, the British accepted the full formal imposition of a French <a href="/wiki/Protectorate" title="Protectorate">protectorate</a> on the island, but French authority was not acknowledged by the government of Madagascar. To force capitulation, the French bombarded and occupied the harbor of <a href="/wiki/Toamasina" title="Toamasina">Toamasina</a> on the east coast, and <a href="/wiki/Mahajanga" title="Mahajanga">Mahajanga</a> on the west coast, in December 1894 and January 1895 respectively.<sup id="cite_ref-Disease_107-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Disease-107">[107]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>A French military <a href="/wiki/Flying_column" title="Flying column">flying column</a> then marched toward Antananarivo, losing many men to malaria and other diseases. Reinforcements came from <a href="/wiki/Algeria" title="Algeria">Algeria</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sub-Saharan_Africa" title="Sub-Saharan Africa">Sub-Saharan Africa</a>. Upon reaching the city in September 1895, the column bombarded the royal palace with heavy artillery, causing heavy casualties and leading Queen Ranavalona III to surrender.<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">[108]</a></sup> France annexed Madagascar in 1896 and declared the island a colony the following year, dissolving the Merina monarchy and sending the royal family into exile on <a href="/wiki/R%C3%A9union" title="RÃ©union">RÃ©union Island</a> and to Algeria. A two-year <a href="/wiki/Menalamba_rebellion" title="Menalamba rebellion">resistance movement</a> organized in response to the French capture of the royal palace was effectively put down at the end of 1897.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">[109]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Under colonial rule, plantations were established for the production of a variety of export crops.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">[110]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Slavery" title="Slavery">Slavery</a> was abolished in 1896 and approximately 500,000 slaves were freed; many remained in their former masters' homes as servants<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">[111]</a></sup> or as sharecroppers; in many parts of the island strong discriminatory views against slave descendants are still held today.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">[112]</a></sup> Wide paved boulevards and gathering places were constructed in the capital city of Antananarivo<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">[113]</a></sup> and the Rova palace compound was turned into a museum.<sup id="cite_ref-FrÃ©migacci_114-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FrÃ©migacci-114">[114]</a></sup> Additional schools were built, particularly in rural and coastal areas where the schools of the Merina had not reached. Education became mandatory between the ages of 6 to 13 and focused primarily on French language and practical skills.<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">[115]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Colonie_de_Madagascar_1897.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Colonie_de_Madagascar_1897.jpg/220px-Colonie_de_Madagascar_1897.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="154" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Colonie_de_Madagascar_1897.jpg/330px-Colonie_de_Madagascar_1897.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Colonie_de_Madagascar_1897.jpg/440px-Colonie_de_Madagascar_1897.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4981" data-file-height="3493"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Colonie_de_Madagascar_1897.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Bond of the French colony Madagascar, issued 7. May 1897
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The Merina royal tradition of <a href="/wiki/Corv%C3%A9e" title="CorvÃ©e">taxes paid in the form of labor</a> was continued under the French and used to construct a railway and roads linking key coastal cities to Antananarivo.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">[116]</a></sup> Malagasy troops fought for France in <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">World War I</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-BGNote_23-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BGNote-23">[23]</a></sup> In the 1930s, <a href="/wiki/Nazi_Germany" title="Nazi Germany">Nazi</a> political thinkers developed the <a href="/wiki/Madagascar_Plan" title="Madagascar Plan">Madagascar Plan</a> that had identified the island as a potential site for the deportation of Europe's Jews.<sup id="cite_ref-contemplation_117-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-contemplation-117">[117]</a></sup> During the <a href="/wiki/Second_World_War" class="mw-redirect" title="Second World War">Second World War</a>, the island was the site of the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Madagascar" title="Battle of Madagascar">Battle of Madagascar</a> between the <a href="/wiki/Vichy_France" title="Vichy France">Vichy French</a> and an <a href="/wiki/Allies_of_World_War_II" title="Allies of World War II">Allied</a> expeditionary force.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">[118]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The occupation of France during the Second World War tarnished the prestige of the colonial administration in Madagascar and galvanized the growing independence movement, leading to the <a href="/wiki/Malagasy_Uprising" title="Malagasy Uprising">Malagasy Uprising</a> of 1947.<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">[119]</a></sup> This movement led the French to establish reformed institutions in 1956 under the <i><a href="/wiki/Loi_Cadre" class="mw-redirect" title="Loi Cadre">Loi Cadre</a></i> (Overseas Reform Act), and Madagascar moved peacefully towards independence.<sup id="cite_ref-Kitchen_1962,_p._256_120-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kitchen_1962,_p._256-120">[120]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Malagasy_Republic" title="Malagasy Republic">Malagasy Republic</a> was proclaimed on 14 October 1958, as an <a href="/wiki/Autonomous_entity" class="mw-redirect" title="Autonomous entity">autonomous</a> state within the <a href="/wiki/French_Community" title="French Community">French Community</a>. A period of provisional government ended with the adoption of a constitution in 1959 and full independence on 26 June 1960.<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">[121]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Independent_state">Independent state</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Madagascar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Independent state">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Malagasy_Republic" title="Malagasy Republic">Malagasy Republic</a>, <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Republic_of_Madagascar" title="Democratic Republic of Madagascar">Democratic Republic of Madagascar</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Third_Republic_of_Madagascar" title="Third Republic of Madagascar">Third Republic of Madagascar</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Philibert_Tsiranana_1962.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/Philibert_Tsiranana_1962.jpg/170px-Philibert_Tsiranana_1962.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="226" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/Philibert_Tsiranana_1962.jpg/255px-Philibert_Tsiranana_1962.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/Philibert_Tsiranana_1962.jpg/340px-Philibert_Tsiranana_1962.jpg 2x" data-file-width="531" data-file-height="705"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Philibert_Tsiranana_1962.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Philibert_Tsiranana" title="Philibert Tsiranana">Philibert Tsiranana</a>, the first <a href="/wiki/List_of_Presidents_of_Madagascar" class="mw-redirect" title="List of Presidents of Madagascar">president of Madagascar</a> (1960â72).
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Since regaining independence, Madagascar has transitioned through four republics with corresponding revisions to its constitution. The <a href="/wiki/Malagasy_Republic" title="Malagasy Republic">First Republic</a> (1960â72), under the leadership of French-appointed President <a href="/wiki/Philibert_Tsiranana" title="Philibert Tsiranana">Philibert Tsiranana</a>, was characterized by a continuation of strong economic and political ties to France. Many high-level technical positions were filled by French expatriates, and French teachers, textbooks and curricula continued to be used in schools around the country. Popular resentment over Tsiranana's tolerance for this "neo-colonial" arrangement inspired a <a href="/wiki/Rotaka" title="Rotaka">series of farmer and student protests</a> that overturned his administration in 1972.<sup id="cite_ref-LOC_29-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LOC-29">[29]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Gabriel_Ramanantsoa" title="Gabriel Ramanantsoa">Gabriel Ramanantsoa</a>, a major general in the army, was appointed interim president and prime minister that same year, but low public approval forced him to step down in 1975. Colonel <a href="/wiki/Richard_Ratsimandrava" title="Richard Ratsimandrava">Richard Ratsimandrava</a>, appointed to succeed him, was assassinated six days into his tenure. General <a href="/wiki/Gilles_Andriamahazo" title="Gilles Andriamahazo">Gilles Andriamahazo</a> ruled after Ratsimandrava for four months before being replaced by another military appointee: Vice Admiral <a href="/wiki/Didier_Ratsiraka" title="Didier Ratsiraka">Didier Ratsiraka</a>, who ushered in the socialist-Marxist <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Republic_of_Madagascar" title="Democratic Republic of Madagascar">Second Republic</a> that ran under his tenure from 1975 to 1993. </p>
      <p>This period saw a political alignment with the <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Bloc" title="Eastern Bloc">Eastern Bloc</a> countries and a shift toward economic insularity. These policies, coupled with economic pressures stemming from the <a href="/wiki/1973_oil_crisis" title="1973 oil crisis">1973 oil crisis</a>, resulted in the rapid collapse of Madagascar's economy and a sharp decline in living standards,<sup id="cite_ref-LOC_29-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LOC-29">[29]</a></sup> and the country had become completely bankrupt by 1979. The Ratsiraka administration accepted the conditions of transparency, anti-corruption measures and free market policies imposed by the International Monetary Fund, <a href="/wiki/World_Bank" title="World Bank">World Bank</a> and various bilateral donors in exchange for their bailout of the nation's broken economy.<sup id="cite_ref-ISS_122-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ISS-122">[122]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Ratsiraka's dwindling popularity in the late 1980s reached a critical point in 1991 when presidential guards opened fire on unarmed protesters during a rally. Within two months, a transitional government had been established under the leadership of <a href="/wiki/Albert_Zafy" title="Albert Zafy">Albert Zafy</a> (1993â96), who went on to win the 1992 presidential elections and inaugurate the <a href="/wiki/Third_Republic_of_Madagascar" title="Third Republic of Madagascar">Third Republic</a> (1992â2010).<sup id="cite_ref-crisisgroup_123-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-crisisgroup-123">[123]</a></sup> The new <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Madagascar" title="Constitution of Madagascar">Madagascar constitution</a> established a multi-party democracy and a separation of powers that placed significant control in the hands of the National Assembly. The new constitution also emphasized human rights, social and political freedoms, and free trade.<sup id="cite_ref-LOC_29-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LOC-29">[29]</a></sup> Zafy's term, however, was marred by economic decline, allegations of corruption, and his introduction of legislation to give himself greater powers. He was consequently impeached in 1996, and an interim president, <a href="/wiki/Norbert_Ratsirahonana" title="Norbert Ratsirahonana">Norbert Ratsirahonana</a>, was appointed for the three months prior to the next presidential election. Ratsiraka was then voted back into power on a platform of decentralization and economic reforms for a second term which lasted from 1996 to 2001.<sup id="cite_ref-ISS_122-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ISS-122">[122]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The contested <a href="/wiki/Malagasy_presidential_election,_2001" class="mw-redirect" title="Malagasy presidential election, 2001">2001 presidential elections</a> in which then-mayor of Antananarivo, Marc Ravalomanana, eventually emerged victorious, caused a seven-month standoff in 2002 between supporters of Ravalomanana and Ratsiraka. The negative economic impact of the political crisis was gradually overcome by Ravalomanana's progressive economic and political policies, which encouraged investments in education and ecotourism, facilitated foreign direct investment, and cultivated trading partnerships both regionally and internationally. National GDP grew at an average rate of 7&nbsp;percent per year under his administration. In the later half of his second term, Ravalomanana was criticised by domestic and international observers who accused him of increasing authoritarianism and corruption.<sup id="cite_ref-ISS_122-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ISS-122">[122]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Opposition leader and then-mayor of Antananarivo, Andry Rajoelina, led a <a href="/wiki/2009_Malagasy_political_crisis" title="2009 Malagasy political crisis">movement in early 2009</a> in which Ravalomanana was pushed from power in an unconstitutional process widely condemned as a <i>coup d'Ã©tat</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">[124]</a></sup> In March 2009, Rajoelina was declared by the Supreme Court as the President of the <a href="/wiki/High_Transitional_Authority" title="High Transitional Authority">High Transitional Authority</a>, an interim governing body responsible for moving the country toward presidential elections. In 2010, a new constitution was <a href="/wiki/Malagasy_constitutional_referendum,_2010" class="mw-redirect" title="Malagasy constitutional referendum, 2010">adopted by referendum</a>, establishing a Fourth Republic, which sustained the democratic, multi-party structure established in the previous constitution.<sup id="cite_ref-crisisgroup_123-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-crisisgroup-123">[123]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Hery_Rajaonarimampianina" title="Hery Rajaonarimampianina">Hery Rajaonarimampianina</a> was declared the winner of the <a href="/wiki/Malagasy_general_election,_2013" class="mw-redirect" title="Malagasy general election, 2013">2013 presidential election</a>, which the international community deemed fair and transparent.<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">[125]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 2018 the first round of the <a href="/wiki/2018_Malagasy_presidential_election" title="2018 Malagasy presidential election">presidential election</a> was held on 7 November and the second round was held on 10 December. Three former presidents and the most recent president were the main candidates of the elections. Former president Andry Rajoelina won the second round of the elections. He was previously president from 2009 to 2014. Former president Marc Ravalomana lost the second round and he did not accept the results because of allegations of fraud. Ravalomana was president from 2002 to 2009. The most recent president Hery Rajaonarimampianina received very modest support in the first round. In January 2019 the High Constitutional Court declared Rajoelina as the winner of the elections and the new president.<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">[126]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">[127]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">[128]</a></sup> In June 2019 <a href="/wiki/2019_Malagasy_parliamentary_election" title="2019 Malagasy parliamentary election">parliamentary elections</a> the party of president Andry Rajoelina won absolute majority of the seats of the National Assembly. It received 84 seats and the supporters of former president Ravalomana got only 16 seats of 151 seats of the National Assembly. 51 seats of deputies were independent or represented small parties. President Rajoelina could rule as a <a href="/wiki/Strongman_(politics)" title="Strongman (politics)">strongman</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">[129]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Government">Government</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Madagascar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Government">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Structure">Structure</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Madagascar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Structure">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Madagascar" class="mw-redirect" title="Government of Madagascar">Government of Madagascar</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Antananarivo05.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Antananarivo05.jpg/220px-Antananarivo05.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Antananarivo05.jpg/330px-Antananarivo05.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Antananarivo05.jpg/440px-Antananarivo05.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2288" data-file-height="1712"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Antananarivo05.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Antananarivo" title="Antananarivo">Antananarivo</a> is the political and economic capital of Madagascar.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Madagascar is a <a href="/wiki/Semi-presidential_system" title="Semi-presidential system">semi-presidential</a> <a href="/wiki/Representative_democracy" title="Representative democracy">representative democratic</a> <a href="/wiki/Diversity_(politics)" title="Diversity (politics)">multi-party</a> republic, wherein the popularly elected president is the head of state and selects a <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Madagascar" title="Prime Minister of Madagascar">prime minister</a>, who recommends candidates to the president to form his cabinet of ministers. According to the <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Madagascar" title="Constitution of Madagascar">constitution</a>, executive power is exercised by the government while legislative power is vested in the ministerial cabinet, the <a href="/wiki/Senate_of_Madagascar" class="mw-redirect" title="Senate of Madagascar">Senate</a> and the <a href="/wiki/National_Assembly_of_Madagascar" class="mw-redirect" title="National Assembly of Madagascar">National Assembly</a>, although in reality these two latter bodies have very little power or legislative role. The constitution establishes independent executive, legislative and judicial branches and mandates a popularly elected president limited to three five-year terms.<sup id="cite_ref-BGNote_23-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BGNote-23">[23]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The public directly elects the president and the 127 members of the National Assembly to five-year terms. All 33 members of the Senate serve six-year terms, with 22 senators elected by local officials and 11 appointed by the president. The last National Assembly election was held on 20 December 2013<sup id="cite_ref-BGNote_23-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BGNote-23">[23]</a></sup> and the last Senate election was held on 30 December 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">[130]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>At the local level, the island's 22 provinces are administered by a governor and provincial council. Provinces are further subdivided into regions and communes. The judiciary is modeled on the French system, with a High Constitutional Court, High Court of Justice, Supreme Court, Court of Appeals, criminal tribunals, and tribunals of first instance.<sup id="cite_ref-justiceMada_131-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-justiceMada-131">[131]</a></sup> The courts, which adhere to <a href="/wiki/Civil_law_(legal_system)" title="Civil law (legal system)">civil law</a>, lack the capacity to quickly and transparently try the cases in the judicial system, often forcing defendants to pass lengthy pretrial detentions in unsanitary and overcrowded prisons.<sup id="cite_ref-mediainfo_132-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mediainfo-132">[132]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Antananarivo is the administrative capital and largest city of Madagascar.<sup id="cite_ref-BGNote_23-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BGNote-23">[23]</a></sup> It is located in the highlands region, near the geographic center of the island. King Andrianjaka founded Antananarivo as the capital of his Imerina Kingdom around 1610 or 1625 upon the site of a captured Vazimba capital on the hilltop of <a href="/wiki/Twelve_sacred_hills_of_Imerina#Hill_of_Analamanga" title="Twelve sacred hills of Imerina">Analamanga</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-vazimbadjp_88-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-vazimbadjp-88">[88]</a></sup> As Merina dominance expanded over neighboring Malagasy peoples in the early 19th century to establish the Kingdom of Madagascar, Antananarivo became the center of administration for virtually the entire island. In 1896 the French colonizers of Madagascar adopted the Merina capital as their center of colonial administration. The city remained the capital of Madagascar after regaining independence in 1960. In 2017, the capital's population was estimated at 1,391,433 inhabitants.<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">[133]</a></sup> The next largest cities are <a href="/wiki/Antsirabe" title="Antsirabe">Antsirabe</a> (500,000), <a href="/wiki/Toamasina" title="Toamasina">Toamasina</a> (450,000) and <a href="/wiki/Mahajanga" title="Mahajanga">Mahajanga</a> (400,000).<sup id="cite_ref-BGNote_23-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BGNote-23">[23]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Politics">Politics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Madagascar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Politics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Madagascar" title="Politics of Madagascar">Politics of Madagascar</a>, <a href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_Madagascar" title="Foreign relations of Madagascar">Foreign relations of Madagascar</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Human_rights_in_Madagascar" title="Human rights in Madagascar">Human rights in Madagascar</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:192px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Andry_Rajoelina_greeting_crowd.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Andry_Rajoelina_greeting_crowd.jpg/190px-Andry_Rajoelina_greeting_crowd.jpg" decoding="async" width="190" height="223" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Andry_Rajoelina_greeting_crowd.jpg/285px-Andry_Rajoelina_greeting_crowd.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Andry_Rajoelina_greeting_crowd.jpg/380px-Andry_Rajoelina_greeting_crowd.jpg 2x" data-file-width="716" data-file-height="839"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Andry_Rajoelina_greeting_crowd.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Madagascar's President <a href="/wiki/Andry_Rajoelina" title="Andry Rajoelina">Andry Rajoelina</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Since Madagascar gained independence from France in 1960, the island's political transitions have been marked by numerous popular protests, several disputed elections, an impeachment, two military coups and one assassination. The island's recurrent political crises are often prolonged, with detrimental effects on the local economy, international relations and Malagasy living standards. The eight-month standoff between incumbent Ratsiraka and challenger Marc Ravalomanana following the 2001 presidential elections cost Madagascar millions of dollars in lost tourism and trade revenue as well as damage to infrastructure, such as bombed bridges and buildings damaged by arson.<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">[134]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/2009_Malagasy_protests" class="mw-redirect" title="2009 Malagasy protests">A series of protests</a> led by Andry Rajoelina against Ravalomanana in early 2009 became violent, with more than 170 people killed.<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">[135]</a></sup> Modern politics in Madagascar are colored by the history of Merina subjugation of coastal communities under their rule in the 19th century. The consequent tension between the highland and coastal populations has periodically flared up into isolated events of violence.<sup id="cite_ref-ethnicstrife_136-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ethnicstrife-136">[136]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Madagascar has historically been perceived as being on the margin of mainstream African affairs despite being a founding member of the <a href="/wiki/Organisation_of_African_Unity" title="Organisation of African Unity">Organisation of African Unity</a>, which was established in 1963 and dissolved in 2002 to be replaced by the <a href="/wiki/African_Union" title="African Union">African Union</a>. Madagascar was not permitted to attend the first African Union summit because of a dispute over the results of the 2001 presidential election, but rejoined the African Union in July 2003 after a 14-month hiatus. Madagascar was again suspended by the African Union in March 2009 following the <a href="/wiki/2009_Malagasy_political_crisis" title="2009 Malagasy political crisis">unconstitutional transfer of executive power</a> to Rajoelina.<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">[137]</a></sup> Madagascar is a member of the <a href="/wiki/International_Criminal_Court" title="International Criminal Court">International Criminal Court</a> with a Bilateral Immunity Agreement of protection for the <a href="/wiki/United_States_military" class="mw-redirect" title="United States military">United States military</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-BGNote_23-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BGNote-23">[23]</a></sup> Eleven countries have established embassies in Madagascar, including France, the United Kingdom, the United States, China and India,<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">[138]</a></sup> while Madagascar has <a href="/wiki/List_of_diplomatic_missions_of_Madagascar" title="List of diplomatic missions of Madagascar">embassies in sixteen other countries</a>. </p>
      <p>Human rights in Madagascar are protected under the constitution and the state is a signatory to numerous international agreements including the <a href="/wiki/Universal_Declaration_of_Human_Rights" title="Universal Declaration of Human Rights">Universal Declaration of Human Rights</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Convention_on_the_Rights_of_the_Child" title="Convention on the Rights of the Child">Convention on the Rights of the Child</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-DOS_139-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DOS-139">[139]</a></sup> Religious, ethnic and sexual minorities are protected under the law. Freedom of association and assembly are also guaranteed under the law, although in practice the denial of permits for public assembly has occasionally been used to impede political demonstrations.<sup id="cite_ref-CrossroadsMarcus_68-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CrossroadsMarcus-68">[68]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-DOS_139-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DOS-139">[139]</a></sup> Torture by security forces is rare and state repression is low relative to other countries with comparably few legal safeguards, although arbitrary arrests and the corruption of military and police officers remain problems. Ravalomanana's 2004 creation of BIANCO, an anti-corruption bureau, resulted in reduced corruption among Antananarivo's lower-level bureaucrats in particular, although high-level officials have not been prosecuted by the bureau.<sup id="cite_ref-CrossroadsMarcus_68-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CrossroadsMarcus-68">[68]</a></sup> Accusations of media <a href="/wiki/Censorship" title="Censorship">censorship</a> have risen due to the alleged restrictions on the coverage of government opposition.<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">[140]</a></sup> Some journalists have been arrested for allegedly spreading <a href="/wiki/Fake_news" title="Fake news">fake news</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">[141]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Security">Security</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Madagascar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Security">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Military_of_Madagascar" class="mw-redirect" title="Military of Madagascar">Military of Madagascar</a>
      </div> 
      <p>The rise of centralized kingdoms among the Sakalava, Merina and other ethnic groups produced the island's first standing armies by the 16th century, initially equipped with spears but later with muskets, cannons and other firearms.<sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">[142]</a></sup> By the early 19th century, the Merina sovereigns of the Kingdom of Madagascar had brought much of the island under their control by mobilizing an army of trained and armed soldiers numbering as high as 30,000.<sup id="cite_ref-army_143-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-army-143">[143]</a></sup> French attacks on coastal towns in the later part of the century prompted then-Prime Minister Rainilaiarivony to solicit British assistance to provide training to the Merina monarchy's army. Despite the training and leadership provided by British military advisers, the Malagasy army was unable to withstand French weaponry and was forced to surrender following an attack on the royal palace at Antananarivo. Madagascar was declared a colony of France in 1897.<sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">[144]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The political independence and sovereignty of the Malagasy armed forces, which comprises an army, navy and air force, was restored with independence from France in 1960.<sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">[145]</a></sup> Since this time the Malagasy military has never engaged in armed conflict with another state or within its own borders, but has occasionally intervened to restore order during periods of political unrest. Under the socialist Second Republic, Admiral Didier Ratsiraka instated mandatory national armed or civil service for all young citizens regardless of sex, a policy that remained in effect from 1976 to 1991.<sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146">[146]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">[147]</a></sup> The armed forces are under the direction of the Minister of the Interior<sup id="cite_ref-justiceMada_131-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-justiceMada-131">[131]</a></sup> and have remained largely neutral during times of political crisis, as during the protracted standoff between incumbent Ratsiraka and challenger Marc Ravalomanana in the disputed 2001 presidential elections, when the military refused to intervene in favor of either candidate. This tradition was broken in 2009, when a segment of the army defected to the side of Andry Rajoelina, then-mayor of Antananarivo, in support of his attempt to force President Ravalomanana from power.<sup id="cite_ref-CrossroadsMarcus_68-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CrossroadsMarcus-68">[68]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The Minister of the Interior is responsible for the national police force, paramilitary force (<i>gendarmerie</i>) and the secret police.<sup id="cite_ref-justiceMada_131-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-justiceMada-131">[131]</a></sup> The police and gendarmerie are stationed and administered at the local level. However, in 2009 fewer than a third of all communes had access to the services of these security forces, with most lacking local-level headquarters for either corps.<sup id="cite_ref-INSTAT_148-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-INSTAT-148">[148]</a></sup> Traditional community tribunals, called <i>dina</i>, are presided over by elders and other respected figures and remain a key means by which justice is served in rural areas where state presence is weak. Historically, security has been relatively high across the island.<sup id="cite_ref-CrossroadsMarcus_68-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CrossroadsMarcus-68">[68]</a></sup> Violent crime rates are low, and criminal activities are predominantly crimes of opportunity such as pickpocketing and petty theft, although child prostitution, human trafficking and the production and sale of marijuana and other illegal drugs are increasing.<sup id="cite_ref-justiceMada_131-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-justiceMada-131">[131]</a></sup> Budget cuts since 2009 have severely impacted the national police force, producing a steep increase in criminal activity in recent years.<sup id="cite_ref-CrossroadsMarcus_68-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CrossroadsMarcus-68">[68]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Administrative_divisions">Administrative divisions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Madagascar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Administrative divisions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Regions_of_Madagascar" title="Regions of Madagascar">Regions of Madagascar</a> and <a href="/wiki/Districts_of_Madagascar" title="Districts of Madagascar">Districts of Madagascar</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Regions_of_Madagascar.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Regions_of_Madagascar.svg/220px-Regions_of_Madagascar.svg.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="399" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Regions_of_Madagascar.svg/330px-Regions_of_Madagascar.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Regions_of_Madagascar.svg/440px-Regions_of_Madagascar.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="803" data-file-height="1458"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Regions_of_Madagascar.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>A map of <a href="/wiki/Regions_of_Madagascar" title="Regions of Madagascar">Madagascar's regions</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Madagascar is subdivided into 22 regions (<i>faritra</i>).<sup id="cite_ref-BGNote_23-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BGNote-23">[23]</a></sup> The regions are further subdivided into 119 districts, 1,579 communes, and 17,485 <i>fokontany</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-INSTAT_148-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-INSTAT-148">[148]</a></sup> </p>

      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Largest_cities_and_towns">Largest cities and towns</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Madagascar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Largest cities and towns">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Agriculture has long influenced settlement on the island. Only 15% of the nation's 24,894,551 population live in the 10 largest cities. </p>
      <p><br> </p>

         <td style="text-align:left;"><a href="/wiki/Analamanga" title="Analamanga">Analamanga</a></td> 
         <td style="text-align:right;">1,275,207 </td> 
         <td rowspan="11" style="text-align: center"><a href="/wiki/File:Lac_Ranomafana.jpg" class="image" title="Antsirabe"><img alt="Antsirabe" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Lac_Ranomafana.jpg/120px-Lac_Ranomafana.jpg" decoding="async" width="120" height="86" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Lac_Ranomafana.jpg/180px-Lac_Ranomafana.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Lac_Ranomafana.jpg/240px-Lac_Ranomafana.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2587" data-file-height="1857"></a><br><a href="/wiki/Antsirabe" title="Antsirabe">Antsirabe</a><br><a href="/wiki/File:Mahajanga_Corniche.jpg" class="image" title="Mahajanga"><img alt="Mahajanga" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Mahajanga_Corniche.jpg/120px-Mahajanga_Corniche.jpg" decoding="async" width="120" height="90" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Mahajanga_Corniche.jpg/180px-Mahajanga_Corniche.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Mahajanga_Corniche.jpg/240px-Mahajanga_Corniche.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3072" data-file-height="2304"></a><br><a href="/wiki/Mahajanga" title="Mahajanga">Mahajanga</a> </td>
