        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/Mahafaly" title="Mahafaly">Mahafaly</a>, <a href="/wiki/Antandroy" title="Antandroy">Antandroy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Antanosy_people" title="Antanosy people">Antanosy people</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bara_people" title="Bara people">Bara</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vezo" class="mw-redirect" title="Vezo">Vezo</a></td> 
         <td>Former <a href="/wiki/Toliara_Province" title="Toliara Province">Toliara Province</a> </td>
        </tr>
       </tbody>
      </table> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Chinese_people_in_Madagascar" title="Chinese people in Madagascar">Chinese</a>, <a href="/wiki/Indians_in_Madagascar" title="Indians in Madagascar">Indian</a> and <a href="/wiki/Comoros" title="Comoros">Comoran</a> minorities are present in Madagascar, as well as a small European (primarily <a href="/wiki/French_people" title="French people">French</a>) populace. Emigration in the late 20th century has reduced these minority populations, occasionally in abrupt waves, such as the exodus of Comorans in 1976, following anti-Comoran riots in Mahajanga.<sup id="cite_ref-LOC_29-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LOC-29">[29]</a></sup> By comparison, there has been no significant emigration of Malagasy peoples.<sup id="cite_ref-EBLand_28-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EBLand-28">[28]</a></sup> The number of <a href="/wiki/French_people_in_Madagascar" class="mw-redirect" title="French people in Madagascar">Europeans</a> has declined since independence, reduced from 68,430 in 1958<sup id="cite_ref-Kitchen_1962,_p._256_120-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kitchen_1962,_p._256-120">[120]</a></sup> to 17,000 three decades later. There were an estimated 25,000&nbsp;Comorans, 18,000&nbsp;Indians, and 9,000&nbsp;Chinese living in Madagascar in the mid-1980s.<sup id="cite_ref-LOC_29-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LOC-29">[29]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Languages">Languages</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Madagascar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Languages">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Madagascar_Kids_5_(4814978342).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Madagascar_Kids_5_%284814978342%29.jpg/220px-Madagascar_Kids_5_%284814978342%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Madagascar_Kids_5_%284814978342%29.jpg/330px-Madagascar_Kids_5_%284814978342%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Madagascar_Kids_5_%284814978342%29.jpg/440px-Madagascar_Kids_5_%284814978342%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1080" data-file-height="720"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Madagascar_Kids_5_(4814978342).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>A Malagasy child
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Malagasy_language" title="Malagasy language">Malagasy language</a> and <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_Madagascar" title="Languages of Madagascar">Languages of Madagascar</a>
      </div> 
      <p>The Malagasy language is of <a href="/wiki/Malayo-Polynesian" class="mw-redirect" title="Malayo-Polynesian">Malayo-Polynesian</a> origin and is generally spoken throughout the island. The numerous dialects of Malagasy, which are generally mutually intelligible,<sup id="cite_ref-194" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-194">[194]</a></sup> can be clustered under one of two subgroups: eastern Malagasy, spoken along the eastern forests and highlands including the Merina dialect of Antananarivo, and western Malagasy, spoken across the western coastal plains. The <a href="/wiki/Malagasy_language" title="Malagasy language">Malagasy language</a> derives from the Southeast <a href="/wiki/Barito_languages" title="Barito languages">Barito languages</a>, with the <a href="/wiki/Ma%27anyan_language" title="Ma'anyan language">Ma'anyan language</a> being its closest relative, incorporating numerous <a href="/wiki/Malay_language" title="Malay language">Malay</a> and <a href="/wiki/Javanese_language" title="Javanese language">Javanese</a> loanwords.<sup id="cite_ref-195" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-195">[195]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-196" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-196">[196]</a></sup> French became the official language during the colonial period, when Madagascar came under the authority of France. In the first national Constitution of 1958, Malagasy and French were named the official languages of the Malagasy Republic. Madagascar is a <a href="/wiki/Francophone" class="mw-redirect" title="Francophone">francophone</a> country, and French is mostly spoken as a second language among the educated population and used for international communication.<sup id="cite_ref-LOC_29-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LOC-29">[29]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>No official languages were mentioned in the Constitution of 1992, although Malagasy was identified as the national language. Nonetheless, many sources still claimed that Malagasy and French were official languages, eventually leading a citizen to initiate a legal case against the state in April 2000, on the grounds that the publication of official documents only in the French language was unconstitutional. The High Constitutional Court observed in its decision that, in the absence of a language law, French still had the character of an official language.<sup id="cite_ref-197" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-197">[197]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In the Constitution of 2007, Malagasy remained the national language while official languages were reintroduced: Malagasy, French, and English.<sup id="cite_ref-198" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-198">[198]</a></sup> English was removed as an official language from the constitution approved by voters in the <a href="/wiki/Malagasy_constitutional_referendum,_2010" class="mw-redirect" title="Malagasy constitutional referendum, 2010">November 2010 referendum</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-4thRepublic_1-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4thRepublic-1">[1]</a></sup> The outcome of the referendum, and its consequences for official and national language policy, are not recognized by the political opposition, who cite lack of transparency and inclusiveness in the way the election was organized by the <a href="/wiki/High_Transitional_Authority" title="High Transitional Authority">High Transitional Authority</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-crisisgroup_123-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-crisisgroup-123">[123]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Madagascar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Religion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_Madagascar" class="mw-redirect" title="Religion in Madagascar">Religion in Madagascar</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="PieChartTemplate thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px"> 
        <div style="background-color:white;margin:auto;position:relative;width:200px;height:200px;overflow:hidden;border-radius:100px;border:1px solid black"> 
         <div style="border:solid transparent;position:absolute;width:100px;line-height:0;left:100px; top:100px; border-width:100px 0 0 5304.5364363156px; border-left-color:Grey"></div> 
         <div style="position:absolute;line-height:0;border-style:solid;left:0;top:0;border-width:0 200px 100px 0;border-color:Grey"></div> 
         <div style="position:absolute;line-height:0;border-style:solid;left:0;top:0;border-width:0 100px 200px 0;border-color:Grey"></div>
         <div style="border:solid transparent;position:absolute;width:100px;line-height:0;left:100px; top:100px; border-width:100px 0 0 205.75905061887px; border-left-color:Green"></div> 
         <div style="position:absolute;line-height:0;border-style:solid;left:0;top:0;border-width:0 200px 100px 0;border-color:Green"></div> 
         <div style="position:absolute;line-height:0;border-style:solid;left:0;top:0;border-width:0 100px 200px 0;border-color:Green"></div>
         <div style="border:solid transparent;position:absolute;width:100px;line-height:0;left:100px; top:100px; border-width:100px 0 0 134.06260318686px; border-left-color:Beige"></div> 
         <div style="position:absolute;line-height:0;border-style:solid;left:0;top:0;border-width:0 200px 100px 0;border-color:Beige"></div> 
         <div style="position:absolute;line-height:0;border-style:solid;left:0;top:0;border-width:0 100px 200px 0;border-color:Beige"></div>
         <div style="border:solid transparent;position:absolute;width:100px;line-height:0;left:100px; top:100px; border-width:100px 0 0 75.57454800484px; border-left-color:Blue"></div> 
         <div style="position:absolute;line-height:0;border-style:solid;left:0;top:0;border-width:0 200px 100px 0;border-color:Blue"></div> 
         <div style="position:absolute;line-height:0;border-style:solid;left:0;top:0;border-width:0 100px 200px 0;border-color:Blue"></div> 
        </div> 
        <div class="thumbcaption"> 
         <p>Religion in Madagascar (2010) according to the <a href="/wiki/Pew_Research_Center" title="Pew Research Center">Pew Research Center</a><sup id="cite_ref-pew_199-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pew-199">[199]</a></sup> </p> 
         <style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r981673959">.mw-parser-output .legend{page-break-inside:avoid;break-inside:avoid-column}.mw-parser-output .legend-color{display:inline-block;min-width:1.25em;height:1.25em;line-height:1.25;margin:1px 0;text-align:center;border:1px solid black;background-color:transparent;color:black}.mw-parser-output .legend-text{}</style>
         <div class="legend">
          <span class="legend-color" style="background-color:Blue; color:white;">&nbsp;</span>&nbsp;<a href="/wiki/Christian" class="mw-redirect" title="Christian">Christian</a> (85.3%)
         </div>
         <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959">
         <div class="legend">
          <span class="legend-color" style="background-color:Beige; color:black;">&nbsp;</span>&nbsp;<a href="/wiki/Animism" title="Animism">Folk religions</a> (4.5%)
         </div>
         <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959">
         <div class="legend">
          <span class="legend-color" style="background-color:Green; color:white;">&nbsp;</span>&nbsp;<a href="/wiki/Muslim" class="mw-redirect" title="Muslim">Muslim</a> (3.0%)
         </div>
         <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959">
         <div class="legend">
          <span class="legend-color" style="background-color:Grey; color:black;">&nbsp;</span>&nbsp;Unaffiliated (6.9%)
         </div> 
        </div> 
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>According to the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_State" title="United States Department of State">U.S. Department of State</a> in 2011, 41% of Madagascans practiced Christianity, and 52% adhered to traditional religions,<sup id="cite_ref-BGNote_23-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BGNote-23">[23]</a></sup> which tends to emphasize links between the living and the <i>razana</i> (ancestors); these numbers were drawn from the 1993 census. According to the <a href="/wiki/Pew_Research_Center" title="Pew Research Center">Pew Research Center</a> in 2010, 85% of the population now practiced <a href="/wiki/Christianity_in_Madagascar" title="Christianity in Madagascar">Christianity</a>, while just 4.5% of Madagascans practiced folk religions; among Christians, practitioners of <a href="/wiki/Protestantism" title="Protestantism">Protestantism</a> outnumbered adherents of <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholicism_in_Madagascar" class="mw-redirect" title="Roman Catholicism in Madagascar">Roman Catholicism</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-pew_199-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pew-199">[199]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Veneration_of_the_dead" title="Veneration of the dead">veneration of ancestors</a> has led to the widespread tradition of tomb building, as well as the highlands practice of the <i><a href="/wiki/Famadihana" title="Famadihana">famadihana</a></i>, whereby a deceased family member's remains are exhumed and re-wrapped in fresh silk shrouds, before being replaced in the tomb. The <i>famadihana</i> is an occasion to celebrate the beloved ancestor's memory, reunite with family and community, and enjoy a festive atmosphere. Residents of surrounding villages are often invited to attend the party, where food and rum are typically served, and a <i><a href="/wiki/Hiragasy" title="Hiragasy">hiragasy</a></i> troupe or other musical entertainment is commonly present.<sup id="cite_ref-famadihana_200-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-famadihana-200">[200]</a></sup> Consideration for ancestors is also demonstrated through adherence to <i><a href="/wiki/Fady_(taboo)" title="Fady (taboo)">fady</a></i>, taboos that are respected during and after the lifetime of the person who establishes them. It is widely believed that by showing respect for ancestors in these ways, they may intervene on behalf of the living. Conversely, misfortunes are often attributed to ancestors whose memory or wishes have been neglected. The sacrifice of <a href="/wiki/Zebu" title="Zebu">zebu</a> is a traditional method used to appease or honor the ancestors. In addition, the Malagasy traditionally believe in a creator god, called <a href="/wiki/Zanahary" title="Zanahary">Zanahary</a> or Andriamanitra.<sup id="cite_ref-Bradtbeliefs_201-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bradtbeliefs-201">[201]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Today, many Christians integrate their religious beliefs with traditional ones related to honoring the ancestors. For instance, they may bless their dead at church before proceeding with traditional burial rites or invite a <a href="/wiki/Minister_(Christianity)" title="Minister (Christianity)">Christian minister</a> to consecrate a <i>famadihana</i> reburial.<sup id="cite_ref-famadihana_200-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-famadihana-200">[200]</a></sup> The Malagasy Council of Churches comprises the four oldest and most prominent Christian denominations of Madagascar (Roman Catholic, <a href="/wiki/Church_of_Jesus_Christ_in_Madagascar" title="Church of Jesus Christ in Madagascar">Church of Jesus Christ in Madagascar</a>, <a href="/wiki/Malagasy_Lutheran_Church" title="Malagasy Lutheran Church">Lutheran</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Church_of_the_Province_of_the_Indian_Ocean" title="Church of the Province of the Indian Ocean">Anglican</a>) and has been an influential force in Malagasy politics.<sup id="cite_ref-USSD_202-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-USSD-202">[202]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">Islam</a> is also practiced on the island. Islam was first brought to Madagascar in the Middle Ages by <a href="/wiki/Arab_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Arab people">Arab</a> and <a href="/wiki/Somali_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Somali people">Somali</a> Muslim traders, who established several Islamic schools along the eastern coast. While the use of Arabic script and loan words and the adoption of Islamic astrology would spread across the island, the Islamic religion took hold in only a handful of southeastern coastal communities. Today, <a href="/wiki/Islam_in_Madagascar" title="Islam in Madagascar">Muslims</a> constitute 3â7&nbsp;percent of the population of Madagascar and are largely concentrated in the northwestern provinces of <a href="/wiki/Mahajanga" title="Mahajanga">Mahajanga</a> and <a href="/wiki/Antsiranana" title="Antsiranana">Antsiranana</a>. The vast majority of Muslims are <a href="/wiki/Sunni" class="mw-redirect" title="Sunni">Sunni</a>. Muslims are divided between those of Malagasy ethnicity, Indians, Pakistanis and Comorans. </p>
      <p>More recently, <a href="/wiki/Hinduism" title="Hinduism">Hinduism</a> was introduced to Madagascar through <a href="/wiki/Gujarati_people" title="Gujarati people">Gujarati people</a> immigrating from the <a href="/wiki/Saurashtra_(region)" title="Saurashtra (region)">Saurashtra</a> region of <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">India</a> in the late 19th century. Most Hindus in Madagascar speak <a href="/wiki/Gujarati_language" title="Gujarati language">Gujarati</a> or <a href="/wiki/Hindi" title="Hindi">Hindi</a> at home.<sup id="cite_ref-id_203-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-id-203">[203]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Madagascar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Madagascar" title="Culture of Madagascar">Culture of Madagascar</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Each of the many ethnic subgroups in Madagascar adhere to their own set of beliefs, practices and ways of life that have historically contributed to their unique identities. However, there are a number of core cultural features that are common throughout the island, creating a strongly unified Malagasy cultural identity. In addition to a common language and shared traditional religious beliefs around a creator god and veneration of the ancestors, the traditional Malagasy worldview is shaped by values that emphasize <i>fihavanana</i> (solidarity), <i>vintana</i> (destiny), <i>tody</i> (karma), and <i><a href="/wiki/Hasina_(Madagascar)" title="Hasina (Madagascar)">hasina</a></i>, a sacred life force that traditional communities believe imbues and thereby legitimates authority figures within the community or family. Other cultural elements commonly found throughout the island include the practice of male circumcision; strong kinship ties; a widespread belief in the power of magic, diviners, astrology and witch doctors; and a traditional division of social classes into nobles, commoners, and slaves.<sup id="cite_ref-LOC_29-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LOC-29">[29]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Bradtbeliefs_201-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bradtbeliefs-201">[201]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Although social castes are no longer legally recognized, ancestral caste affiliation often continues to affect social status, economic opportunity, and roles within the community.<sup id="cite_ref-204" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-204">[204]</a></sup> Malagasy people traditionally consult <i>Mpanandro</i> ("Makers of the Days") to identify the most auspicious days for important events such as weddings or <i>famadihana</i>, according to a traditional astrological system introduced by Arabs. Similarly, the nobles of many Malagasy communities in the pre-colonial period would commonly employ advisers known as the <i>ombiasy</i> (from <i>olona-be-hasina</i>, "man of much virtue") of the southeastern <a href="/wiki/Antemoro_people" title="Antemoro people">Antemoro</a> ethnic group, who trace their ancestry back to early Arab settlers.<sup id="cite_ref-205" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-205">[205]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The diverse origins of Malagasy culture are evident in its tangible expressions. The most emblematic instrument of Madagascar, the <i><a href="/wiki/Valiha" title="Valiha">valiha</a></i>, is a <a href="/wiki/Bamboo" title="Bamboo">bamboo</a> <a href="/wiki/Tube_zither" title="Tube zither">tube zither</a> carried to Madagascar by early settlers from <a href="/wiki/South_Kalimantan" title="South Kalimantan">southern Borneo</a>, and is very similar in form to those found in <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Indonesia" title="Music of Indonesia">Indonesia</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Music_of_the_Philippines" title="Music of the Philippines">Philippines</a> today.<sup id="cite_ref-Blench,_R._1982_pp._81-93_206-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Blench,_R._1982_pp._81-93-206">[206]</a></sup> Traditional <a href="/wiki/Architecture_of_Madagascar" title="Architecture of Madagascar">houses in Madagascar</a> are likewise similar to those of southern Borneo in terms of symbolism and construction, featuring a rectangular layout with a peaked roof and central support pillar.<sup id="cite_ref-207" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-207">[207]</a></sup> Reflecting a widespread veneration of the ancestors, tombs are culturally significant in many regions and tend to be built of more durable material, typically stone, and display more elaborate decoration than the houses of the living.<sup id="cite_ref-Acquier,_Jean-Louis._208-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Acquier,_Jean-Louis.-208">[208]</a></sup> The production and weaving of silk can be traced back to the island's earliest settlers, and Madagascar's national dress, the woven <i><a href="/wiki/Lamba_(garment)" title="Lamba (garment)">lamba</a></i>, has evolved into a varied and refined art.<sup id="cite_ref-209" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-209">[209]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The Southeast Asian cultural influence is also evident in <a href="/wiki/Malagasy_cuisine" title="Malagasy cuisine">Malagasy cuisine</a>, in which rice is consumed at every meal, typically accompanied by one of a variety of flavorful vegetable or meat dishes.<sup id="cite_ref-Antal_210-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Antal-210">[210]</a></sup> African influence is reflected in the sacred importance of zebu cattle and their embodiment of their owner's wealth, traditions originating on the African mainland. <a href="/wiki/Cattle_raiding" title="Cattle raiding">Cattle rustling</a>, originally a rite of passage for young men in the plains areas of Madagascar where the largest herds of cattle are kept, has become a dangerous and sometimes deadly criminal enterprise as herdsmen in the southwest attempt to defend their cattle with traditional spears against increasingly armed professional rustlers.<sup id="cite_ref-Camp93_85-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Camp93-85">[85]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Arts">Arts</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Madagascar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Arts">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Madagascar" title="Music of Madagascar">Music of Madagascar</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Hira_gasy_dancer_Madagascar.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/Hira_gasy_dancer_Madagascar.jpg/170px-Hira_gasy_dancer_Madagascar.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="278" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/Hira_gasy_dancer_Madagascar.jpg/255px-Hira_gasy_dancer_Madagascar.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/Hira_gasy_dancer_Madagascar.jpg/340px-Hira_gasy_dancer_Madagascar.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2272" data-file-height="3712"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Hira_gasy_dancer_Madagascar.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>A <a href="/wiki/Hiragasy" title="Hiragasy">Hiragasy</a> dancer.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>A wide variety of oral and written <a href="/wiki/Literature_of_Madagascar" title="Literature of Madagascar">literature</a> has developed in Madagascar. One of the island's foremost artistic traditions is its oratory, as expressed in the forms of <i><a href="/wiki/Hainteny" title="Hainteny">hainteny</a></i> (poetry), <i>kabary</i> (public discourse) and <i>ohabolana</i> (proverbs).<sup id="cite_ref-211" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-211">[211]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Madatana_212-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Madatana-212">[212]</a></sup> An epic poem exemplifying these traditions, the <i><a href="/wiki/Ibonia" title="Ibonia">Ibonia</a></i>, has been handed down over the centuries in several different forms across the island, and offers insight into the diverse mythologies and beliefs of traditional Malagasy communities.<sup id="cite_ref-213" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-213">[213]</a></sup> This tradition was continued in the 20th century by such artists as <a href="/wiki/Jean-Joseph_Rabearivelo" title="Jean-Joseph Rabearivelo">Jean-Joseph Rabearivelo</a>, who is considered Africa's first modern poet,<sup id="cite_ref-214" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-214">[214]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Elie_Rajaonarison" title="Elie Rajaonarison">Elie Rajaonarison</a>, an exemplar of the new wave of Malagasy poetry.<sup id="cite_ref-215" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-215">[215]</a></sup> Madagascar has also developed a rich <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Madagascar" title="Music of Madagascar">musical heritage</a>, embodied in dozens of regional musical genres such as the coastal <i><a href="/wiki/Salegy" title="Salegy">salegy</a></i> or highland <i><a href="/wiki/Hiragasy" title="Hiragasy">hiragasy</a></i> that enliven village gatherings, local dance floors and national airwaves.<sup id="cite_ref-Randrianary_216-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Randrianary-216">[216]</a></sup> Madagascar also has a growing culture of classical music fostered through youth academies, organizations and orchestras that promote youth involvement in classical music. </p>
      <p>The plastic arts are also widespread throughout the island. In addition to the tradition of silk weaving and lamba production, the weaving of <a href="/wiki/Raffia_palm" title="Raffia palm">raffia</a> and other local plant materials has been used to create a wide array of practical items such as floor mats, baskets, purses and hats.<sup id="cite_ref-handicrafts_176-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-handicrafts-176">[176]</a></sup> Wood carving is a highly developed art form, with distinct regional styles evident in the decoration of balcony railings and other architectural elements. Sculptors create a variety of furniture and household goods, <i>aloalo</i> funerary posts, and wooden sculptures, many of which are produced for the tourist market.<sup id="cite_ref-Terrible_217-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Terrible-217">[217]</a></sup> The decorative and functional woodworking traditions of the <a href="/wiki/Zafimaniry" title="Zafimaniry">Zafimaniry</a> people of the central highlands was inscribed on UNESCO's <a href="/wiki/UNESCO_Intangible_Cultural_Heritage_Lists" title="UNESCO Intangible Cultural Heritage Lists">list of Intangible Cultural Heritage</a> in 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-218" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-218">[218]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Among the Antaimoro people, the production of paper embedded with flowers and other decorative natural materials is a long-established tradition that the community has begun to market to eco-tourists.<sup id="cite_ref-Terrible_217-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Terrible-217">[217]</a></sup> Embroidery and <a href="/wiki/Drawn_thread_work" title="Drawn thread work">drawn thread work</a> are done by hand to produce clothing, as well as tablecloths and other home textiles for sale in local crafts markets.<sup id="cite_ref-handicrafts_176-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-handicrafts-176">[176]</a></sup> A small but growing number of fine art galleries in Antananarivo, and several other urban areas, offer paintings by local artists, and annual art events, such as the Hosotra open-air exhibition in the capital, contribute to the continuing development of fine arts in Madagascar.<sup id="cite_ref-219" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-219">[219]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sport">Sport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Madagascar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Sport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Moraingy_fighting_Madagascar_sport.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Moraingy_fighting_Madagascar_sport.jpg/220px-Moraingy_fighting_Madagascar_sport.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="177" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Moraingy_fighting_Madagascar_sport.jpg/330px-Moraingy_fighting_Madagascar_sport.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Moraingy_fighting_Madagascar_sport.jpg/440px-Moraingy_fighting_Madagascar_sport.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1617" data-file-height="1301"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Moraingy_fighting_Madagascar_sport.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><i><a href="/wiki/Moraingy" title="Moraingy">Moraingy</a></i> is a traditional martial art of Madagascar.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>A number of traditional pastimes have emerged in Madagascar. <i><a href="/wiki/Moraingy" title="Moraingy">Moraingy</a></i>, a type of hand-to-hand combat, is a popular spectator sport in coastal regions. It is traditionally practiced by men, but women have recently begun to participate.<sup id="cite_ref-220" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-220">[220]</a></sup> The wrestling of <a href="/wiki/Zebu" title="Zebu">zebu</a> cattle, which is named savika or <i>tolon-omby</i>, is also practiced in many regions.<sup id="cite_ref-lambatradition_221-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lambatradition-221">[221]</a></sup> In addition to sports, a wide variety of games are played. Among the most emblematic is <i><a href="/wiki/Fanorona" title="Fanorona">fanorona</a></i>, a board game widespread throughout the Highland regions. According to folk legend, the succession of King <a href="/wiki/Andrianjaka" title="Andrianjaka">Andrianjaka</a> after his father <a href="/wiki/Ralambo" title="Ralambo">Ralambo</a> was partially the result of the obsession that Andrianjaka's older brother may have had with playing <i>fanorona</i> to the detriment of his other responsibilities.<sup id="cite_ref-iarivo_222-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-iarivo-222">[222]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Western recreational activities were introduced to Madagascar over the past two centuries. <a href="/wiki/Rugby_union_in_Madagascar" title="Rugby union in Madagascar">Rugby union</a> is considered the national sport of Madagascar.<sup id="cite_ref-223" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-223">[223]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Football_in_Madagascar" title="Football in Madagascar">Soccer</a> is also popular. Madagascar has produced a world champion in <a href="/wiki/P%C3%A9tanque" title="PÃ©tanque">pÃ©tanque</a>, a French game similar to <a href="/wiki/Lawn_bowling" class="mw-redirect" title="Lawn bowling">lawn bowling</a>, which is widely played in urban areas and throughout the Highlands.<sup id="cite_ref-224" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-224">[224]</a></sup> School athletics programs typically include soccer, track and field, judo, boxing, women's basketball and women's tennis. Madagascar sent its first competitors to the <a href="/wiki/1964_Summer_Olympics" title="1964 Summer Olympics">Olympic Games</a> in 1964, and has also competed in the <a href="/wiki/African_Games" title="African Games">African Games</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-EBLand_28-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EBLand-28">[28]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Scouting" title="Scouting">Scouting</a> is represented in Madagascar by its <a href="/wiki/Firaisan%27ny_Skotisma_eto_Madagasikara" title="Firaisan'ny Skotisma eto Madagasikara">own local federation</a> of three scouting clubs. Membership in 2011 was estimated at 14,905.<sup id="cite_ref-Census_2010_225-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Census_2010-225">[225]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Because of its advanced sports facilities, Antananarivo gained the hosting rights for several of Africa's top international basketball events, including the <a href="/wiki/2011_FIBA_Africa_Championship" class="mw-redirect" title="2011 FIBA Africa Championship">2011 FIBA Africa Championship</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-226" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-226">[226]</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/2009_FIBA_Africa_Championship_for_Women" title="2009 FIBA Africa Championship for Women">2009 FIBA Africa Championship for Women</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-227" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-227">[227]</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/2014_FIBA_Africa_Under-18_Championship" title="2014 FIBA Africa Under-18 Championship">2014 FIBA Africa Under-18 Championship</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-228" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-228">[228]</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/2013_FIBA_Africa_Under-16_Championship" title="2013 FIBA Africa Under-16 Championship">2013 FIBA Africa Under-16 Championship</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-229" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-229">[229]</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/2015_FIBA_Africa_Under-16_Championship_for_Women" title="2015 FIBA Africa Under-16 Championship for Women">2015 FIBA Africa Under-16 Championship for Women</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-230" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-230">[230]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Madagascar%27s_national_3x3_basketball_team" class="mw-redirect" title="Madagascar's national 3x3 basketball team">Madagascar's national 3x3 basketball team</a> won the gold medal at the <a href="/wiki/3x3_basketball_at_the_2019_African_Games" title="3x3 basketball at the 2019 African Games">2019 African Games</a>. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cuisine">Cuisine</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Madagascar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Cuisine">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Malagasy_cuisine" title="Malagasy cuisine">Malagasy cuisine</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Malagasy cuisine reflects the diverse influences of <a href="/wiki/List_of_Asian_cuisines" title="List of Asian cuisines">Southeast Asian</a>, <a href="/wiki/African_cuisine" title="African cuisine">African</a>, <a href="/wiki/Indian_cuisine" title="Indian cuisine">Indian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chinese_cuisine" title="Chinese cuisine">Chinese</a> and <a href="/wiki/European_cuisine" title="European cuisine">European</a> culinary traditions. The complexity of Malagasy meals can range from the simple, traditional preparations introduced by the earliest settlers, to the refined festival dishes prepared for the island's 19th-century monarchs. Throughout almost the entire island, the contemporary cuisine of Madagascar typically consists of a base of rice (<i>vary</i>) served with an accompaniment (<i>laoka</i>). The many varieties of <i>laoka</i> may be <a href="/wiki/Vegetarian_cuisine" title="Vegetarian cuisine">vegetarian</a> or include animal proteins, and typically feature a sauce flavored with such ingredients as ginger, onion, garlic, tomato, vanilla, coconut milk, salt, curry powder, green peppercorns or, less commonly, other spices or herbs. In parts of the arid south and west, pastoral families may replace rice with maize, <a href="/wiki/Cassava" title="Cassava">cassava</a>, or <a href="/wiki/Curd" title="Curd">curds</a> made from fermented zebu milk. A wide variety of sweet and savory <a href="/wiki/Fritter" title="Fritter">fritters</a> as well as other street foods are available across the island, as are diverse tropical and temperate-climate fruits. Locally produced beverages include fruit juices, coffee, herbal teas and teas, and alcoholic drinks such as <a href="/wiki/Rum" title="Rum">rum</a>, wine, and beer.<sup id="cite_ref-Antal_210-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Antal-210">[210]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Three_Horses_Beer" title="Three Horses Beer">Three Horses Beer</a> is the most popular beer on the island<sup id="cite_ref-THBpilsner_231-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-THBpilsner-231">[231]</a></sup> and is considered emblematic of Madagascar.<sup id="cite_ref-promos_232-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-promos-232">[232]</a></sup> The island also produces some of the world's finest chocolate; <a href="/wiki/Chocolaterie_Robert" title="Chocolaterie Robert">Chocolaterie Robert</a>, established in 1940, is the most famous chocolate company on the island.<sup id="cite_ref-prize_233-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-prize-233">[233]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Madagascar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
